- **Abdominal swelling:** Decoct with *shengma* (cimicifuga).
- **Lumbar swelling:** Decoct with *tinglizi* (lepidium).
- **Limb swelling:** Decoct with *sangbaipi* (mulberry root bark).
- **Leg swelling:** Wash 1 pinch of raw rice, grind, steep in boiling water, and use the liquid to swallow the pills.

If severe diarrhea occurs, soak the hands and feet in cold water to stop it. This medicine must **never** be taken by women during pregnancy or after childbirth. It should be taken at dawn on an empty stomach.

For swelling in the feet and knees, after taking the medicine, lie down with both legs raised to allow the water to flow toward the feet, discharging through urination and defecation, which will naturally reduce the swelling. On the day of administration, no other medicines should be taken. **Avoid licorice entirely**, and abstain from salt for half a year to prevent recurrence.

This medicine should not be taken in excess, nor should it be taken daily. If a single dose fails to expel all the water, administer it once every three days. On the remaining two days, take a decoction of *Shengliao Wuling San* and *Jiahe San* combined, prepared with ginger and jujube, to regulate the spleen, stimulate appetite, and promote diuresis, thereby resolving the swelling.

**For bloody stool:**
- Burn *wumei* (mume fruit) to preserve its properties, then form into pills with vinegar-cooked rice paste, to be taken with either hot water or wine.
- Alternatively, dry-fry *huanglian* (coptis) and *baizhi* (cypress leaf), grind into powder, and take on an empty stomach with wine.
- Another method: Grind *jingjiesui* (schizonepeta spike) and *sharen* (amomum fruit) into powder. Take 3 *qian* per dose with glutinous rice water, three times daily.
- Another remedy: Grind *wubeizi* (gallnut) into powder, mix with salted mume to form a paste, and shape into *wutong*-sized pills. Take 50 pills per dose with either wine or hot water.

**For bloody diarrhea:**
- Use *baiyaojian* (nutgall), half burned to ash and half raw, ground into powder and formed into soft rice pills. Take 30 pills per dose with rice water.

**For intestinal wind, hemorrhoids, and fistula:**
- Soak *baizhi* (angelica) in rice water overnight, then slice and place on heated earth (swept clean of ash). Cover with paper and dry over low heat. Grind into powder and take daily with wine.
- Alternatively, remove the seeds and skin from *zaojiao* (Chinese honey locust), honey-fry, and grind into powder. Form into pills with rice paste and swallow with rice water.
- Another method: Dry-fry *canger* leaves or seeds, grind into powder, and take with honey.

**Topical washes and applications:**
- Dissolve *poxiao* (mirabilite) in well water for washing. For application, mix with honey, *jisu* (catnip) pills, and *poxiao*.
- Another formula: Grind *tongqing* (verdigris), *mituoseng* (litharge), and a small amount of *shexiang* (musk) into powder, mix with saliva, and apply.

**For protruding hemorrhoids causing difficulty in sitting or standing (rapid and miraculous effect):**
- Wash *jiucai* (Chinese leek) thoroughly, steep in boiling water in a ceramic or wooden vessel, and use the steam to fumigate, followed by washing with the liquid.
- Alternatively, boil watermelon rind until fragrant and use the steam for fumigation and washing as above.
- Another method: Slice fresh ginger thinly and place on the painful hemorrhoids. Form *shu’ai* (processed mugwort) into cones and place on the ginger, then moxa three times. Yellow fluid will discharge, and the swelling will subside. If two or three hemorrhoids are present, repeat the process every three to five days. This method has been repeatedly proven effective.

**For rectal prolapse:**
- Mix *wulongwei* (soot from roof beams) with mouse droppings, burn to produce smoke in a bucket, and sit over it to fumigate. After several treatments, the prolapse will cease.

**For cough:**
- *Renshen* (ginseng, remove rhizome)
- *Fangfeng* (saposhnikovia, remove rhizome)
- *Banxia* (pinellia, soaked in water)
- *Gancao* (licorice)
- *Chenpi* (aged tangerine peel, remove pith, stir-fry)
- *Jiegeng* (platycodon, remove rhizome, stir-fry)
- *Xingren* (apricot kernel, remove skin and tip)
- *Mahuang* (ephedra, remove nodes)
- *Sangbaipi* (mulberry root bark, remove coarse skin, stir-fry)
- *Zisu* (perilla)
- *Douluo* (poria, remove veins, stir-fry; if unavailable, substitute *suqiao* [poppy husk], remove membrane, stir-fry until dry)
- *Wumei* (mume fruit, half per dose)

Grind equal parts of the above ingredients, then decoct 3 *qian* with five slices of ginger until reduced to seven parts. Strain and take the liquid orally before retiring at the end of the first watch (around 9–11 PM). The decoction may be taken with or without the dregs, and the remaining portion may be consumed the following night. Adjust the formula based on the severity of the condition:

- For consumptive cough, add *wuweizi* (schisandra).
- For heat in the five centers (palms, soles, and chest), add *digupi* (wolfberry root bark).
- For dry mouth, add *renshen* (ginseng) and *menghdong* (ophiopogon).
- For excessive phlegm, add *nanxing* (prepared arisaema).
- For abdominal distension, add stir-fried *zhiqiao* (bitter orange peel).
- For chest fullness, add *zhiqiao*.
- For lung distension, add stir-fried *sangbaipi*.
- For constipation, add *dafupi* (areca peel).
- For frequent nightmares, add *renshen* and *yuanzhi* (polygala, remove core).
- For inability to lower the head, add *kutingli* (lepidium).
- For wheezing, lumbar pain, and weakness in the knees and feet, add *mugua* (chaenomeles) and *wuyao* (lindera).
- For numbness in the hands and feet, add *wuyao* and *fangji* (stephania).
- For cold-induced cough, add *ganjiang* (dried ginger), *rougui* (cinnamon), and *xixin* (asarum).
- For loss of voice, add *hezi* (chebule) and *bohe* (mint).

If coughing persists upon onset, decoct *Jiubao Yin* (Nine-Treasure Drink) with boy’s urine and take.

- For hemoptysis, add *maohua* (cogongrass flower) and *ounie* (lotus rhizome node).
- For coughing up blood-streaked sputum, add *puhuang* (cattail pollen) and *maohua* (burned to ash and added to the decoction).
- For coughing up pink sputum, add *baihe* (lily bulb), *wubeizi* (gallnut), and *maohua* (all burned to preserve properties).
- For poor appetite, add *baishaoyao* (white peony) and *baimu* (white wood), decocted with ginger and jujube.
- For sudden hemoptysis and heat in the five centers, decoct *Fuling Buxin Tang* (Poria Heart-Nourishing Decoction) with *maohua* and *puhuang*.
- For dry throat and mouth, add *renshen* and *gegan* (kudzu).
- For cold damage with aversion to wind, wheezing, and cough, decoct *Xiao Qinglong Tang* (Minor Blue Dragon Decoction).
- For seasonal colds, use *Jin Feicao San* (Inula Powder) with *sangbaipi* and *suqiao*.
- For wind-induced cough with headache, add *chuanxiong* (ligusticum) and *baizhi* (angelica), decocted with ginger and scallion.
- For cold damage with fever and cough, omit *suqiao* and add *chaihu* (bupleurum) and *huangqin* (scutellaria).
- For tidal fever with cough, decoct *Shen Su Yin* (Ginseng-Perilla Drink) slowly and take.

Pregnant women should only take *Baihe San* (Lily Powder).

When burning ingredients to ash, place them in a small cup and pour the decoction over them to take together. After taking this medicine, follow with *Pinglao Wan* (Fatigue-Relieving Pill) on an empty stomach with rice water.

**Avoid the following when treating cough:** raw or cold foods, salty or sour flavors, roasted or fried foods, greasy or oily dishes, wine, wheat-based foods, lamb, duck, fish, seafood, tofu, and sexual activity.

**Renshen Jiaolong San (Ginseng Dragon-Intersecting Powder) for persistent cough:**
- *Renshen* (ginseng)
- *Ejiao* (ass hide glue, stir-fried)
- *Kuandonghua* (coltsfoot)
- *Suqiao* (poppy husk, stir-fried with rice)

Grind the above ingredients in equal parts. For each dose, take three *qian*, decoct with one dark plum, and take at midnight.

**Er Mu San (Two Mothers Powder) for acute wheezing, inability to lie flat, and profuse phlegm and saliva:**
- *Zhimu* (anemarrhena rhizome)
- *Beimu* (fritillaria bulb)

Grind the two ingredients into powder and take before sleep, mixed with warm plain boiled water. For acute wheezing, add *kutingli* (tingli seed) powder. For persistent cough, add *douling* (stephania root) powder; if unavailable, substitute with poppy husk, removing the veins and membranes without processing.

**Hei Long Wan (Black Dragon Pill) to dissolve phlegm and treat cough, regardless of age or duration:**
- *Mingfan* (alum, calcined) – one *liang*
- *Chifan* (green vitriol, calcined) – one *liang*
- *Nanxing* (arisaema, prepared) – two *qian*
- *Baiyaojian* (sumac gallnut) – two *qian*

- *Banxia* (pinellia, prepared) – two *qian*

Grind into powder and form into *wutong*-seed-sized pills with flour paste. For each dose, take thirty pills: for cold-type cough, take before sleep with light ginger decoction; for heat-type cough, take at bedtime with tea.

**Hua Tan Yuan (Phlegm-Dissolving Pill):**
- *Mingfan* (alum, calcined) – one *qian*
- *Nanxing* (arisaema, half raw, half prepared)
- *Banxia* (pinellia, soaked)

Grind into powder, form into small *wutong*-seed-sized pills with ginger juice paste, and take twenty to thirty pills after meals with ginger decoction.

**Jiuben Yi Nian Jin (Old Edition One-Pinch Gold):**
- *Zhimu* (anemarrhena rhizome) – one *liang*
- *Beimu* (fritillaria bulb) – one *liang*
- *Badou* (croton seed, oil removed) – ten seeds

Grind finely and mix evenly with the above. For each dose, take a pinch, dip onto both sides of three ginger slices, chew thoroughly while lying in bed, and swallow before sleep—relief will come immediately, and the next day there will be a bowel movement. Children should take half the dose.

**For loss of voice:**
- *Zaojiao* (honey locust, skin and seeds removed) – one stick
- Radish – three, sliced

Simmer together in one bowl of water until reduced to half a bowl. No more than three doses are needed to restore speech.

**For nosebleed:**
- Radish juice – half a cup
- Wine – half a cup

Mix evenly, warm in hot water, and take—effective.

Another formula: Burn a woman’s hair to ash, mix evenly with *xiangfuzi* (cyperus) powder, and take with hot water.

Another formula: Burn *zhizi* (gardenia) to preserve its nature, grind into powder, and insufflate into the nostrils—immediate relief.

Another formula: *Yujin* (turmeric) powder, decoct *baimaohua* (cogongrass flower) and take with the decoction.

Another formula: Roll axle grease into pills and insert into the nostrils—highly effective.

**Ru Shen Dan (Divine Elixir) for unbearable head wind and headache:**
- *Guangming liuhuang* (bright sulfur) – one *liang*
- *Xiaoshi* (niter) – one *liang*

Grind together finely, form into finger-sized water pills, and chew on an empty stomach with tea.

Another formula: **San Ling San (Three Spirits Powder)** for eight types of head wind:
- *Cao wu* (wild aconite) and *xixin* (asarum) in equal parts
- A small amount of *huangdan* (yellow lead)

Grind into an extremely fine powder and insufflate into the nostrils.

**Ying Xu Yuan Jun Tou Feng Dan (Immortal Ying Xu’s Head Wind Elixir):**
- *Da chuanwu* (Sichuan aconite) – two *liang*, boiled in river water once, drained, then boiled again in a clean place seven times, sliced, and stir-fried with salt until yellow
- *Liao xixin* (Manchurian wild ginger) – four *liang*, roots and soil removed, soaked in wine
- A small amount of *shexiang* (musk)
- *Gao xi cha ya* (high-grade tea buds) – half a *jin*

Grind into powder. For each dose, take three *qian* after meals or before sleep, mixed with tea. Shortly after, take hot water to induce sweating or nasal discharge until relief.

**For heart and spleen qi pain:**
- *Guixin* (cinnamon heart) – grind into powder and take with plain boiled water or wine.

Another formula: *Wancansha* (silkworm sand) in any amount, steep in boiling water, strain, and take the clear liquid—immediate relief.

Another formula: *Xuanhusuo* (corydalis) and *hujiao* (pepper) powder, taken with wine.

**Shen Ying San (Divine Response Powder) for small intestine qi pain:**
- *Xuanhusuo* (corydalis)
- *Hujiao* (pepper)

Grind into powder. For each dose, take two *qian*, decocted in half a cup of wine and half a cup of water.

**For swelling and hardness of the small intestine and bladder:**
- *Xiangfuzi* (cyperus) powder, taken with a decoction of *haizao* (seaweed).

Another formula: **Si Sheng San (Four Sages Powder)** for hernia and swollen external genitals:
- *Huixiang* (fennel, stir-fried)
- *Chuan shanjia* (pangolin scales, stir-fried)
- *Quanxie* (scorpion, stir-fried)
- *Nan muxiang* (costus root)

Grind equal parts into powder. For each dose, take two *qian* with wine—pain will cease after one dose, highly effective.

Another formula: Take a handful of *denglongcao* (Chinese lantern plant) with stems and leaves, place in a pot with a piece of crushed raw ginger and raw wine, and decoct. Take warm on an empty stomach.

Another formula: Remove *rougui* (cinnamon) from *Wuling San* (Five-Ingredient Powder with Poria) and add *heiqianniu* (black morning glory), *jiegeng* (platycodon), and *cheqianzi* (plantain seed)—called *Pan Cong San* (Coiled Onion Powder). Several doses are highly effective.

Another formula: *Huixiang* (fennel), *ruxiang* (frankincense) powder, *zhuling* (polyporus), *jiegeng* (platycodon), *mutong* (akebia), and *gancao* (licorice) in equal parts, decocted with a handful of *dengxin* (rush pith) and *danzhuye* (lophatherum)—take frequently for effect.

**For unilateral sagging hernia:**
First take *Fuyuan Tongqi San* (Qi-Restoring Powder), then *Wuling San* (Five-Ingredient Powder with Poria), each three *qian*, removing *rougui* (cinnamon) and adding equal parts of *heiqianniu* (black morning glory) and *wuzhuyu* (evodia, soaked in wine). For distension, add *chen zhiqiao* (aged bitter orange, lightly stir-fried with wheat bran); for severe pain, add *bajiao huixiang* (star anise) and decoct.

**For purple patch wind (purpura):**
- *Liuhuang* (sulfur) – one *liang*, boiled in vinegar for a day
- *Haipiaoxiao* (cuttlebone) – three pieces

Grind together into powder. After bathing, dip fresh ginger into the powder and rub thoroughly on the affected area. Avoid wind for a short time—several applications will cure it completely.

Another formula: Rub *zhimu* (anemarrhena) with vinegar.

**For spitting or coughing blood:**
- *Cebaiye* (oriental arborvitae leaf), baked dry on a tile, ground into powder, and taken with rice water—three *qian* per dose, effective after three to five doses.

Another formula: *Lianye* (lotus leaf), baked dry and ground into powder, taken with rice water—about two *qian* per dose.

Another formula: Drink fresh, warm urine.

Another formula: *Guodi mo* (soot from a wok, calcined), ground finely and taken with well water.

**For bone lodged in the throat:**
- *Ruxiang* (frankincense) – two *qian*, ground finely and swallowed with water in small sips.

Another formula: Hold *shatang* (rock sugar) in the mouth and swallow slowly—the bone will descend on its own.

Another formula: Decoct *zhugen* (ramie root, used for making cloth) with the meat of the animal whose bone is lodged.

Another formula: Chew and swallow *susharen* (cardamom) and *gancao* (licorice) dry.

Another formula: Swallow *poxiao* (mirabilite).

For fish bones lodged in the throat, place a fish bone atop the crown of the head—the bone will descend. Another formula: regardless of whether the bone is from chicken or fish, grind *poxiao* (mirabilite) finely, mix with *jisu* (catnip), and form into pills the size of a marble. Lie supine and hold three to five pills in the mouth to dissolve—the bone will naturally dissipate.

For accidental swallowing of a needle, hold a piece of *cishi* (magnetite) in the mouth, and the needle will emerge. Another method: consume a large quantity of fatty pork or mutton, and it will pass through the stool.

For children who accidentally swallow coins, burn charcoal until red-hot, then promptly grind it into powder and decoct in water. Sip the liquid for immediate effect.

For lodged iron, stone, bone, or splinters in dire cases, grind equal parts *wangbuliuxing* (vaccaria seeds) and *huangbai* (phellodendron bark, with coarse skin removed) into powder, mix with steamed cake, and form into pills the size of a marble. Coat with *qingdai* (indigo), thread with string, and hang in a windy place. For each dose, dissolve one pill in cold water and administer.

For venomous snakebites, promptly drink one or two bowls of good vinegar to prevent the poison from spreading with the blood, or consume one or two cups of clear oil as an alternative. Then apply medicine, or first bind the wound tightly with a headband at both ends. Next, take *baizhi* (angelica root) powder, mix with plain water, and consume about half a *liang*—soon after, yellow fluid will drain from the bite, the swelling will subside, and the skin will close. Another formula: apply *xionghuang* (realgar) powder topically. Another: dissolve and consume it in water. Another formula: grind equal parts *baifan* (alum), *xionghuang* (realgar), and *huangla* (yellow wax) into powder, form into pills the size of a fingertip, and melt one on a spoon over heat when treating a bite. Drip the melted liquid onto the wound, or use a bamboo tube to direct it inward—the poison will not spread, which is especially effective.

For insects entering the ear, pound leek juice with vinegar and pour into the ear. Another method: warm peach leaves over fire and plug the ear—the insect will emerge immediately. Another: pour clear oil into the ear, and the insect will exit. Another: cut a rooster’s comb and drip the blood into the ear.

For bleeding from the ear, blow *longgu* (dragon bone) powder into the ear, or use calcined *baifan* (alum) mixed with *shexiang* (musk) and blow it in to stop the bleeding.

For ears that are persistently moist, discharging pus or yellow fluid:
- *Huangdan* (lead oxide) – one *qian*, stir-fried
- *Chishaoyao* (red peony root) – two and a half *qian*
- *Lingxiaohua* (campsis flower) – two and a half *qian*

Grind all into powder and blow into the ear. If the condition does not improve, add:
- *Baifan* (alum) – one *qian*, calcined
- *Yanzhi* (rouge) – a pinch
- *Wubeizi* (gallnut) – two and a half *qian*, baked
- *Quanxie* (scorpion) – whole, baked

Grind into powder and blow into the ear—the ear will dry.

For long-term deafness with no hearing.

For long-term deafness with no hearing:
Take a piece of *cishi* (magnetite) the size of a soybean, and a pinch of *shexiang* (musk). Seal them in a bamboo tube with *tuohe* oil (camel-goose oil). Wrap in fresh cotton and insert into the affected ear, while holding a small piece of raw iron in the mouth. When a sound like wind or rain is felt inside the ear, the condition will be cured. Repeat three to five times for full effect.

For bites from venomous insects:
Make a large paper wick, dip it in sesame oil, and light it as a lamp. Hold the flame near the wound to fumigate it—the poison will be drawn into the lamp’s smoke.

For abdominal pain caused by accidentally swallowing a leech:
Form clay into pills and swallow them with water. The leech will be expelled with the clay in the stool.

For spider sores:
Apply sheep’s milk to the affected area, or rub with clear oil to soothe it.

For rabid dog bites:
Pound scallion roots to extract the juice and consume a large amount. Alternatively, decoct *taobaipi* (white bark of the peach tree) and drink the liquid, or apply moxibustion to the wound three to five times. Another method: grind *zhen danfan* (true chalcanthite) into powder and apply it to the wound for immediate healing.

For centipede bites:
Chew *zhuyu* (evodia fruit) and rub it on the bite. Alternatively, apply chicken droppings, or mix ginger juice with *bangfen* (freshwater clam powder) and apply. Another method: cut into mulberry tree bark to extract the sap and apply it for immediate healing. If the pain is unbearable, apply moxibustion to the wound three to five times. Another remedy: light a lamp with clear oil and rush pith, then use the smoke to fumigate the bite—this will stop the pain. This method is also effective for other venomous insect bites and is highly reliable.

For wasp stings:
Wash the sting with warm wine for immediate relief, or apply clear oil.

For tiger wounds:
First drink a bowl of clear oil, then wash the wound with oil. Alternatively, decoct *gan’ge* (kudzu root) in water and use it to wash the wound. Another method: mix brown sugar with water and apply it to the wound, while also drinking one or two bowls of brown sugar water.

For snakebite remedies:
Grind the following into powder:
- *Xixin* (asarum) – five *qian*
- *Baizhi* (angelica) – five *qian*
- *Xionghuang* (realgar) – two and a half *qian*

Add a small amount of *shexiang* (musk). Take two *qian* per dose, mixed with warm wine. Another remedy: grind *beimu* (fritillaria) into powder, mix with cold wine, and drink as much as possible. Use aged wine, as it will cause clear fluid to flow from the wound. Once the fluid is fully discharged, apply the dregs of the medicine to the wound for healing.

For scalds and burns:
Grind charcoal into a paste with water and apply, or grind *tuzhu* (cinnabar) and apply. Alternatively, apply pure tung oil. Another method: pound *baiye* (cypress leaves) into a paste and apply to the painful area, or pound *huangshukui* (yellow hollyhock) flowers and leaves and apply. For all scalds and burns, immediately warm the affected area by the fire. Though painful, endure it for the duration of a meal, and the pain will cease. Do not apply cold water or cold objects, as this will trap heat and cause the flesh to rot—guard against this.

For cuts and axe wounds with unstoppable bleeding and unbearable pain:
Stir-fry scallion whites in a wok until hot, then pound them into a paste. Apply while hot and bind securely—the pain and bleeding will stop immediately. Replace with fresh scallions when they cool. Alternatively, pound scallion leaves into a paste, stir-fry until hot, and apply. Another method: grind aged lime into a fine powder, mix with an equal amount of *dahuang* (rhubarb), and stir-fry until the mixture turns pink. Apply to the wound. Another remedy: calcine and grind *guodi mo* (soot from the bottom of a wok) and apply. Another method: grind *baiji* (bletilla) and calcined *shigao* (gypsum) together into powder and sprinkle on the wound to close it. Another remedy: apply *wumingyi* (no-name mineral) powder.

For sprains and strains causing pain in the hands and feet:
Pound fresh ginger into a paste, mix with flour, stir-fry until hot, and consume. Adding scallion whites enhances the effect.

For foreign objects lodged in the eye:
Grind high-quality ink with clear water and apply a drop to the corner of the eye—the object will come out.

For ears discharging pus or fluid:
Blow powdered raw *baifan* (alum) into the ear three times a day for immediate effect.

For needles, iron, bamboo, or wood splinters lodged in the flesh:
Grind ten or more pieces of dried sheep droppings into powder, mix with water, and apply thickly to the affected area. The pain will cease, and the splinter will emerge on its own. Another method: chew the yellow part of a chestnut and apply. Another remedy for bamboo or wood splinters: grind black soybeans into a paste, mix with water, and apply. Another method: grind *bimazi* (castor bean) kernels into a paste. First place a piece of silk over the wound, then apply the medicine, checking frequently. When the splinter emerges, remove the medicine to avoid damaging healthy flesh. Adding *baimei* (dried plum) flesh and grinding together before application is also effective.

For chapped hands and feet in winter:
Mix *baiji* (bletilla) powder with water and fill the cracks. Avoid contact with water for three to five days.

For frostbite on the heels in cold weather:
On the fifth day of the fifth lunar month at noon, rub the affected area with ginger, scallions, and mugwort for about an hour—it will never recur.

For toothache:
Decoct a handful of *qinghao* (sweet wormwood) in a bowl of water until half remains. Rinse the mouth with the warm liquid to stop the pain. Another remedy: grind *liangjiang* (galangal) and *caowu* (wild aconite) into powder and rub it on the teeth. Spit out any saliva—do not swallow. After spitting, rinse the mouth with salt water. Another remedy: for tooth decay or wind-induced toothache, take appropriate medicine based on whether the condition is yin, yang, deficient, or excess. In spring, use *Zhengqi San* (Rectify Qi Powder); in summer, add *dahuang* (rhubarb) and *zhiqiao* (bitter orange peel) to *Baidusan* (Antiphlogistic Powder); in autumn and winter, use *Wujisan* (Five Accumulations Powder) or *Xiaofeng San* (Eliminate Wind Powder). To eliminate parasitic accumulations: grind *binglang* (areca nut) into powder, mix with honey water, and take on an empty stomach. Have the patient eat lightly the day before, skip dinner, and take the medicine at dawn the next day.

For palm abscesses:
Pound fresh mulberry leaves into a paste and wrap the affected area for healing.

*Xianchuan Waike Mifang*, Volume Ten, Concluded
*Variant notes: #1 "Gan" (干) in the original is written as "Qian" (千) in the manuscript. #2 The character "二" is absent in the manuscript. #3 After "染," the manuscript includes the character "淀." #4 "脓" was originally written as "浓," corrected per the manuscript. #5 "筋" is suspected to be a miswriting of "箸." #6 "汁" in the manuscript is written as "汗." #7 The missing character in the original is "皆" in the manuscript. #8 "羊" is suspected to be a miswriting of "王."*

*Xianchuan Waike Mifang*, Volume Eleven
Compiled by Zhaoyi Yuanyangzi of Junyi

**Treatise on Miscellaneous Disorders**

**For Children’s Ailments**

For vexing heat in the five centers with thirst and desire to drink, boil black soybeans and feed them to the child to bring peace.

For chronic convulsions with lethargy and occasional spasms, grind *lindera root* (乌药) into water and administer warm.

For acute or chronic convulsions in children, grind together twenty grains of *Zhenling Dan* (震灵丹), ten grains of *Laifu Dan* (来复丹), and ten grains of *Bai Yuanzi* (白圆子). Form into pills the size of mung beans using glutinous rice paste. Administer five pills for older children and three for younger ones. For chronic convulsions, use a decoction of northern jujubes and tangerine peel to swallow the pills; for acute convulsions, use fresh ginger juice with boiling water.

**Ten Types of Cinnabar Toxins in Children**
Master Xu states: These ten types of cinnabar toxins, if left untreated for three days, will invade the intestines and stomach, becoming incurable. Carefully distinguish each type and treat accordingly with these formulas—failure is rare.

1. **Flying Hearth Cinnabar (飞灶丹)**: Swelling with a glossy appearance starting from the crown of the head. Pound scallion whites to extract their natural juice and apply.
2. **Auspicious Hearth Cinnabar (吉灶丹)**: Red, swollen, and painful starting from the head. Apply a mixture of red adzuki bean powder and egg white.
3. **Ghost Fire Cinnabar (鬼火丹)**: Red swelling starting from the face. Mix *heart of the hearth* soil (宠心土) with egg white and apply.
4. **Heavenly Fire Cinnabar (天火丹)**: Red spots starting from the back. Apply a mixture of mulberry root bark powder and sheep fat.
5. **Heavenly Hearth Cinnabar (天灶丹)**: Yellowish-red swelling starting from both arms. Apply a mixture of willow wood ash and water.
6. **Water Cinnabar (水丹)**: Hollow swelling starting from both flanks. Apply a mixture of iron filings and pig dung.
7. **Barbarian Secondary Cinnabar (胡次丹)**: Yellow swelling starting from above the navel. Apply a mixture of areca nut powder and rice vinegar.
8. **Wildfire Cinnabar (野火丹)**: Red swelling starting from both legs. Apply a mixture of frankincense powder and sheep fat.
9. **Smoke Fire Cinnabar (烟火丹)**: Red and white spots starting from both legs. Apply a mixture of soil from beneath a pig trough and sesame oil.
10. **Barbarian Leaking Cinnabar (胡漏丹)**: Yellow swelling starting from the genitals. Apply a mixture of soil from a leaky roof and sheep fat.

**For Infantile Head Sores, Fetal Toxins, Various Wind-Heat Malignancies, and Pox Sores**
*Huangbai* (黄柏), *Huanglian* (黄连), *Baizhi* (白芷), and *Wu Bei Zi* (五倍子). Grind equal parts of these four ingredients into a fine powder. Mix with well water to an appropriate consistency, spread in a bowl, and place it atop two bricks with a gap beneath. Burn mugwort (*Ai*) to fumigate with its smoke until the mixture turns black and dry. Remove the medicine, grind it again into powder, and mix with clear oil for application. If worms are present, use boiled oil for application.

Another formula: Grind equal parts *Wu Bei Zi* and *Baizhi* into powder. For weeping sores, sprinkle the powder to absorb the pus. For dry sores, mix with clear oil and apply.

**For Pox-Related Eye Afflictions in Children**
Grind *Gujingcao* (谷精草) into powder and administer with white persimmon, pig liver, or malt sugar.

**Shengxi Fuming San (生犀复明散)**, for various eye disorders:
*Red peony root* (赤芍药) 2 liang, *Scutellaria* (黄芩) 1 liang, *Akebia stem* (木通) 2 liang, *Mulberry root bark* (桑白皮) 2 liang, *Gentian* (龙胆草) 2 liang, *Saposhnikovia* (防风) 2 liang, *Notopterygium* (羌活) 2 liang, *Tangkuei tails* (当归尾) 2 liang, *Rhubarb* (大黄) 8 qian, *Bitter orange peel* (枳壳, with the inner membrane removed) 6 qian.
Crush the ingredients, and for each dose, take 5 qian with 1.5 cups of water. Add a small amount of fresh mulberry root bark and decoct to 80% of the original volume. Administer after meals. For red eyes with thick obstructions, add raw clam powder; for painful swelling, add raw rehmannia for efficacy.

**Eye Drops**
Wash *Huanglian* (宣黄连) thoroughly, chop, and decoct in a ceramic vessel until reduced by half. Strain the liquid, place it in a ceramic bowl over a steamer, and evaporate until the liquid is minimal. Add a small amount of borneol, store in a clean container or horn tube, and apply to the eyes. It is also effective for festering canthi. When preparing the medicine, strain through fine silk to ensure no dust or debris remains.

**For Sudden Redness and Festering Canthi**
*Huanglian* (黄连) 5 qian, *Tangkuei tails* (当归尾) 3 qian, *Mirabilite* (朴消) 3 qian, *Apricot kernel* (板杏) 2 qian, *Huangbai* (黄柏) 2 qian, *Teasel root* (川续断) 1 qian.
Crush the ingredients, place in a bowl over a steamer, and steam thoroughly. While hot, dip and apply the juice to the eyes.

Another method for red eyes and dim, painful vision: Keep the eyes tightly closed, scoop hot water with the hands, and pour it over the eyes. Stop when the water cools. Repeat frequently—relief lies in keeping the eyes closed.

**For Obstructions and Films in the Eyes**
Dissolve 10 liang of pure *Mirabilite* (朴消) in hot water, strain through a bamboo basket lined with fine paper, and collect in a ceramic bowl. Heat over charcoal until dry, then place on the ground overnight. Add 2 liang of processed *Yellow Lead* (黄丹) and half a qian of musk, grind finely, sift through silk, and add borneol. Apply to the eyes.

**Fumigation for Sudden Red Eyes**
Decoct *Bohe* (薄荷), *Jingjie* (荆芥), and *Fangfeng* (防风) in a ceramic pot. Fumigate the eyes with the hot vapor, then wash with the hands.

**Huangu Dan (换骨丹)**, for wind-dampness, lumbar, and leg disorders:
Grind 6 liang of *Cao Wu* (草乌, slightly removing the skin and tips) into powder. Mix with 2 liang of fresh tofu to form cakes, boil in water until they float, then remove. The boiling must be precise—overcooking weakens the medicine, while undercooking makes it too potent. Soak 3 liang of *Cang Zhu* (苍术) in rice-washed water, dry over a fire, and add 1 liang of pure *Tianma* (天麻) and half a liang of washed and lightly fried *Quan Xie* (全蝎). Grind these with the *Cao Wu* cakes into powder, form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds using rice paste. In the evening, avoid eating; before bed, chew *Mugua* (木瓜) and take twenty pills with warm wine. When the medicine permeates the body and feet by midnight, a numbing sensation indicates its efficacy.

**Shujin San (舒筋散)**, for blood stasis, muscle spasms, joint pain, and difficulty walking—this is the foremost formula for invigorating blood and transforming qi:
*Corydalis* (玄胡索), *Tangkuei* (当归), *Cinnamon bark* (官桂).
Grind equal parts into powder. Take 2 qian per dose with warm wine on an empty stomach.

**Huoluo Dan (活络丹)**, for all ailments of the waist and legs:
Four liang of *Huluba* (胡芦巴); two liang stir-fried with four liang of *Haijinsha* (海金沙) until the latter is spent, and two liang stir-fried with four liang of *Badou* (巴豆) until red. *Haijinsha* is commonly called "bamboo garden dung"; gather it in the eighth or ninth month, wrap it in paper-lined baskets, dry in the sun, then tap with bamboo to dislodge the seeds, discarding the leaves. (Beware of counterfeits sold by merchants—use only whole *Badou*, shelled.) Four liang of *Cang’ercao* (苍耳草), dried over fire (commonly called "wild eggplant leaf"; in the *Bencao*, it is *Xi’er*). Four liang of *Zuochanteng* (左缠藤), leaves and all, dried over fire.
Grind the three ingredients into powder, form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds using a paste of fine wine and wheat flour. Swallow thirty to forty pills with unheated wine. For waist ailments, take while half-hungry; for knee and leg ailments, take on an empty stomach.

**Plaster Formula for All Sores:**
Boil one jin of clear oil with two liang of human hair until melted. Add, as desired, half a liang each of *Gancao* nodes (甘草节), *Danggui* tails (当归尾), *Huanglian* (黄连), *Badou* (巴豆), *Bimazi* (蓖麻子), *Huangualou* (黄瓜篓), and *Mubiezi* (木鳖子). Boil twice, strain, then add five liang of *shuifen* (水粉). Boil again until bubbling, then add seven liang of *Huangdan* (黄丹). Boil once more until bubbling, then add one liang of *Ruxiang* powder (乳香末). Stir constantly with peach and willow twigs until droplets form pearls in water and do not stick to the hand—then the plaster is ready.

**Alternative Plaster Formula:**
Boil five liang of sesame oil with twenty-eight *Badou* (巴豆) and twenty-eight cun of willow twigs until the *Badou* turns black. Strain, then gradually add two liang of *Gudan* (谷丹), stirring constantly with willow twigs. When droplets form unbroken beads in water and do not stick to the hand, remove from heat. Blend in one qian of *Ruxiang* powder, store in a ceramic vessel, and apply once cooled.

**Shen Shou Xiang Su San (神授香苏散)**, for seasonal epidemics:
As the formula’s preface states: Once, during a great plague in the city, a white-haired elder taught a wealthy household to prepare and distribute this remedy, curing all the afflicted. Later, plague ghosts questioned the household, and when told the truth, they exclaimed, "This elder has saved three cities!"—then bowed and departed. Those who take this medicine must abstain from meat, fish, wine, and rich foods; none will fail to recover.

During the former Yuan dynasty, a severe epidemic struck Taihe County in Jian, Jiangxi. A physician returning from house calls late at night suddenly encountered a divine figure on horseback with an entourage. Sensing the figure was no mortal, the physician prostrated himself. The deity halted and demanded, "Who are you?" The physician replied, "I am a physician." The deity asked, "What medicines do you use to treat illness?" The physician answered, "I adjust formulas based on the patient’s cold, heat, and severity." The deity said, "That is not so. For all cases, *Xiang Su San* is best." The physician returned home and, the next day, followed the deity’s instructions—all were cured. His medical practice flourished, bringing him lifelong fortune and reverence for the deity. This account is recorded here.

*Xiangfuzi* (香附子), stir-fried to remove fuzz—four liang
*Purple perilla leaves* (紫苏叶)—four liang
*Chenpi* (陈皮)—one liang
*Gancao* (甘草), roasted—one liang
Chop coarsely, grind into powder. For each dose, steep three qian in one cup of water, decoct to seven parts, strain, and take warm at any time, three times daily.

**Xian Fang San Bu Wan (仙方三补丸)**, a supreme supplement for all deficiencies and debilities, effective for young and old alike:
Two liang of *Poguzhi* (破故纸), stir-fried between paper until fragrant and cooked
One liang of *Baifuling* (白茯苓), peeled
One liang of *Moyao* (没药), steeped in ash-free wine
When the wine has dissolved the *Moyao* to a syrup-like consistency, grind the first two ingredients into powder, form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds using the medicated wine paste. Take twenty to thirty pills on an empty stomach with warm water.

The *Xian Fang* states: Once, a man who took this medicine retained a youthful appearance into old age. *Poguzhi* supplements the kidneys, *Fuling* nourishes the heart, and *Moyao* nourishes the blood. When these three are robust, the body naturally thrives.

**For Jaundice from Wine (酒疸脾黄):**
Grind *Mubiezi* (木鳖子) with vinegar and take one or two cups—relief will follow.

**For Unstoppable Night Sweats:**
Fill the navel with *Wubeizi* (五倍子) powder mixed with saliva, bind with a cloth, and leave overnight—sweating will cease.

**For Genital Sweating:**
Wash *Huangqi* (绵黄芪), slice thinly, place in a pot, and stir-fry with wine until dry and brittle. Grind into powder and take with boiled pig’s heart—marvelously effective.

**Alternative Formula:**
Grind equal parts *Shechuangzi* (蛇床子) and *Shichangpu* (石菖蒲) into powder and apply two or three times daily.

**For Acne (痤疿):**
Cut a fresh cucumber and rub the affected area, or bathe with a decoction of jujube leaves.

**Alternative Formula:**
Mix four liang of *Yuyingfen* (玉英粉) and *Zhenbangfen* (真蚌粉) with one liang of *Huashi* (滑石) and two liang of *Lüdoufen* (绿豆粉), then apply the powder dry.

**For □□ (gagging):**
Use *Bimazi* (蓖麻子) as needed—remove the coarse shells, stir-fry until cooked. Eat the sweet ones; spit out the bitter ones. Eating more brings quicker results.

**For Sudden Tongue Swelling Protruding from the Mouth (due to centipede venom):**
Cut the comb of a rooster, collect the blood in a ceramic dish, and immerse the tongue in it—swallowing will cause the tongue to retract.

**For Delirium, Seeing Ghosts, or Madness:**
Add *Chensha* powder (辰砂末) to *Pingwei San* (平胃散) and take with jujube decoction.

**For Chronic "Pig Cold Wind" Syndrome (猪寒风证), *Rusheng San* (如圣散) is effective for men and women of any age:**
Equal parts of:
*Weilingxian* (威灵仙)
*Fangfeng* (防风)
*Jingjie* (荆芥)
*Fangji* (防己)
*Mahuang* (麻黄)
*Xingren* (杏仁)
*Xixin* (细辛)
*Chuanxiong* (川芎)
*Baizhi* (白芷)
Chop, then decoct with three slices of ginger in fine wine and take warm at the onset of symptoms. Later, roast a large *Huangjingchai* (黄荆柴) over fire, collect the liquid from both ends, mix with aged wine, and swallow *Jinbo Zhenxin Wan* (金箔镇心丸). Avoid foods that provoke wind or toxins.

**On Great Wind (大风):**
*Xiaoranzi’s* Treatise on Great Wind
Great Wind manifests in myriad ways, often arising from excessive desires and the depletion of blood and qi...

Or from pent-up rage, sorrow, fright, or repressed emotions that cannot be released; or from bodily weakness and porous skin; or from drinking wine while exposed to wind; or from stripping off clothes while sweating, then entering water; or from bathing and immediately facing wind; or from drunkenly sleeping in the open; or from wounds on hands or feet that admit wind-toxins; or from sudden storms, cold water, or damp obstructions that invade the flesh—if one is afflicted in the moment, it may lead to the suffering of Great Wind. The disease’s causes spread through the channels and network vessels, transmit to the viscera and bowels, emerge in the four limbs, and steam both internally and externally, forming blistering ringworm.

The origins of this illness comprise three syndromes and five mortal stages. The first syndrome is Water Wind; the second, Transmission and Transformation; the third, self-neglect through lack of regulation. The five mortal stages are: first, Skin Death—numbness and loss of sensation; second, Flesh Death—insensitivity to cutting; third, Blood Death—festering and suppuration; fourth, Sinew Death—shedding of hands and feet; fifth, Bone Death—collapse of the nasal bridge, loss of eyes, eversion of lips, leading to loss of voice, beyond all remedy.

The Five Winds are: first, Wind afflicting the Lung Channel, where the eyebrows fall first; second, Wind afflicting the Liver Channel, where the face erupts in purple blisters; third, Wind afflicting the Kidney Channel, where the soles of the feet perforate first; fourth, Wind afflicting the Spleen Channel, where the entire body becomes scaly like ringworm; fifth, Wind afflicting the Heart Channel, where the eyes are first damaged.

Some cases arise from ancestral gravesites or residences, transmitted in succession among parents, spouses, or household members. Others stem from carelessness outside—latrines, bedchambers, bedding, clothing, or resting beneath bridges or trees—where fate aligns with baleful stars, and one contracts this vile malady, mired in its filth. The manifestations vary, the suffering unbearable, and those who seek treatment often find no relief. Some die within a year or half a year.

In all cases of this affliction, early intervention is essential for ease of cure. One must carefully examine and distinguish the conditions, for if treatment errs even slightly, the consequences may be as vast as the difference between a hair’s breadth and a thousand miles. Alas, even skilled physicians and learned scholars often recoil from its repulsiveness and pay it little heed.

Some unlearned individuals recklessly pass down their techniques, wielding blades and needles to draw blood at will, burning arsenic or moxa to fumigate and induce salivation, or applying toxic herbs steeped in oil to the body. Those who submit to such treatments find no efficacy in a hundred cases. Even if there is slight temporary relief, the affliction recurs over time, and without encountering a superior formula or wondrous medicine, the patient may ultimately die of the disease.

When seeking medical treatment, one must first reside in a quiet chamber, abstain from alcohol and sexual activity, purify the mind and cleanse the heart, and sincerely repent before the divine physician. Additionally, one must avoid exposure to wind and the stirring of qi, as well as refrain from consuming meat, fish, salt, fermented sauces, raw or cold foods. Patience and composure are essential. Only then may one take various medicines, adjusting dosages as needed, preparing pills and powders, and administering them according to the prescribed method—thereby ensuring a cure without fail.

First, administer purgative pills to expel foul blood. If pus or festering sores are present, use medicinal washes for fumigation and cleansing. Within ten days, healthy flesh will emerge. Old sores will gradually recede and cease to erupt, the ears and nose will regain their openness, the skin will feel refreshed, eyebrows and beard will regrow, the complexion will become radiant, and the five viscera will be harmonized. The efficacy of these treatments defies full description.

The formulas are as follows:

**Disperse Wind Powder (Day 1)**
*Fragrant Angelica (1 tael), Scorpion (1 tael, tips removed), Ginseng (1 tael)*
Grind into powder. Take two mace each dose at noon, consuming only congee. Avoid ginger, pepper, and all heating substances. Refrain from eating supper. The next morning, take the powder on an empty stomach, mixed with warm wine, and delay breakfast. Mild dryness of the skin is desirable.

**Expel Wind Powder (Purgative for Blood, Day 2)**
*Rhubarb (6 taels), Sichuan Curcuma (1.8 taels, smaller roots preferred), Gleditsia Thorn (1 tael)*
Grind into powder. Begin with a dose of six, seven, or five mace, adding two and a half mace of *Da Feng* oil, a small amount of refined mirabilite, and mix with a bowl of well-brewed wine (not hot, but lukewarm). Do not eat congee in the evening. Wait until the *Xu* hour (7–9 p.m.), place a bowl of warm water in a basin on the table, and add a small amount of sugar or honey decoction to a plate—ensuring the patient does not see the medicine beforehand. After taking the medicine, have the patient rinse their mouth with water, then sweeten it with the honey decoction. They must not lie down; instead, have someone accompany them while sitting for a long while. Severe abdominal pain is most desirable, and purging ten or more times is unproblematic. Afterward, consume thin congee to restore strength.

This purgative is generally unsuitable for the elderly or weak; those under fifty may be treated. For the robust, administer three doses within ten days: on the first day, *Disperse Wind Powder*; the second day, *Expel Wind Powder*; the third day, *Grind Wind Pill*; the fourth day, *Disperse Wind Powder* again; the fifth day, *Expel Wind Powder*; and the sixth day, *Grind Wind Pill*. For the frail, administer one dose within ten days. Once some improvement is seen, follow the regimen for the robust, taking one dose every ten days after two months. Carefully note the days.

**Grind Wind Pill (Day 3, two doses daily)**
*Sichuan Angelica, Notopterygium, Pubescent Angelica, Sichuan Lovage (smaller roots), Gastrodia, Asarum, Saposhnikovia, Schizonepeta, Clematis, Ephedra (nodes removed), Fleeceflower Root, Tribulus, Arctium, Toad Leaf, Cocklebur, Ground Pine*
Sixteen ingredients, each one tael. Dry in the sun, grind into powder (avoid fire), and form into pills the size of firmiana seeds using wine-cooked rice paste. Take thirty pills per dose, before or after meals, twice daily.

**Wash Formula**
*Lycium Bark, Schizonepeta, Sophora, Asarum (3 taels each)*
Chop and mix evenly. Use two taels per wash, decocted in river water. Fumigate and wash the entire body; bleeding indicates efficacy. For washing, use a large tub or vat with ample water to fully immerse the body for an extended period.

**Topical Application (Day 4, for severe festering sores)**
*Eucommia (2 taels, firm), Sulfur (6 mace), Calcined Alum (2 taels), Cnidium (4 taels), Calcite (2 taels), a small amount of Mirabilite*
Grind into fine powder and mix with lard or sesame oil for application. If sores are not festering, washing is unnecessary.

**Supplementary Formula (from alternate texts) for all wind afflictions, numbness of flesh, itchy skin, scabies, leprosy, ringworm, various sores, rashes, facial wind resembling crawling insects, purple or white patches, or kidney wind attacking the legs and feet causing sores—all may be treated with this.**
*Shiny Dark Plant (2 taels), Angelica (1 tael), Fleeceflower Root (3 taels), Angelica (2 taels), Sophora (2 taels), Clematis (2 taels, rhizomes removed), Tribulus (1.5 taels), Pubescent Angelica (1 tael), Lovage (1 tael), Saposhnikovia (2 taels), Schizonepeta (2 taels), Notopterygium (1 tael), Red Peony (1 tael), Tribulus (1 tael, stir-fried), Earthworm (3 taels, soil removed), Typhonium (1 tael), Gardenia (1 tael), Black-Striped Snake (1, soaked in good wine, steamed until dry, bones removed, flesh dried or baked)*
Grind the above into powder, then add:
*Sesame (2 taels, stir-fried), Chaulmoogra (3 taels, shelled)*
Grind these two together, mix with the previous powder, and form into pills the size of firmiana seeds using wine-cooked rice paste. Take thirty to forty pills per dose, with tea or wine.

**Additional Formula**
*Clematis, Fleeceflower Root, Ground Pine, Saposhnikovia, Tribulus, Schizonepeta, Toad Leaf, Asarum, Arctium, Gleditsia Thorn, Angelica, Cocklebur, Gastrodia, Licorice (honey-fried), Notopterygium, Pubescent Angelica, Ephedra (nodes removed), Bugleweed, Sichuan Lovage, Sophora*

Grind the above ingredients in equal parts into powder, decoct together, and form into pills with rice paste, the size of firmiana seeds. Take forty to fifty pills per dose, with tea or wine as preferred.

**Additional Formula for Regrowing Eyebrows**
Roast Gleditsia Thorn until dry and char Deer Antler to preserve its nature, each in equal parts. Grind into fine powder, mix with fresh ginger juice, and apply to the eyebrows once daily. Eyebrows will naturally regrow.

**Moxibustion Method for Radical Cure**
At the crease between the tendon and bone of the big toe, and at the joints of the fingers—approximately half an inch in length—moxa each point three times to expel toxic qi.

*End of Scroll Eleven, Esoteric Formulas of the Immortal’s External Medicine*

**Appendix: The Power of Convenience in Action**
In this world, convenience is paramount; when strength permits, act without delay, for missed opportunities are to be regretted. Those with wealth and power wield immense influence over others’ fortunes. In all matters, let convenience guide your heart: grant one measure of leniency, and others receive one measure of blessing. Go further—perform good deeds of every kind without pause. Emulate the sages who sought to benefit all under heaven; no greater merit exists.

**First among great conveniences is the equitable sale of grain.**
The Celestial Master Zhang of Han taught that the foremost merit lies in saving lives. Those with means should, at harvest time, purchase grain in abundance—or store their own surplus—and release it at the original price during shortages. This costs them nothing yet brings immense benefit to others. The late Huang Chengshi of Chengdu practiced this and was honored by the Purple Palace Perfected Lord Zhang; he ascended to immortality, and his family enjoyed prosperity for generations. Even better is to sell grain at a reduced price during times of scarcity.

**Second is the relief of illness—a great convenience.**
Those who devoutly prepare and distribute the *Ruyi Elixir* of Perfected Lord Xu can cure myriad diseases, especially epidemics. Other efficacious remedies are also commendable, as is the printing and distribution of proven formulas.

**Third, in summer, provide cool water; in winter, offer clothing to the elderly and infirm.**
Care for widows, orphans, the childless, and the solitary. Foster abandoned children. Provide coffins for the unburied. Aid those in sudden distress or dire need as circumstances allow.

**Fourth, deliverance of the departed is a small effort with vast merit.**
Master Ge ascended through this practice, and Perfected Lady Sa likewise attained immortality. All past immortals and masters prioritized this; those who regularly perform sacrificial refinement bring blessings to the departed. Even offering a single meal confers no small benefit.

**Enlightened individuals and upright scholars** delve deeply, seeking to comprehend the illusory nature of life and destiny and to master the alchemy of water and fire. They not only transcend the mundane but also deliver the departed. Merit and virtue begin here, but one must seek a teacher’s guidance to avoid squandering the opportunity.

**Fifth, all living beings share the capacity for suffering.**
Where possible, refrain from killing. Treat insects, birds, and beasts with the same compassion. Daoist scriptures prescribe fasting and releasing life on the Three Officials’ festivals, for on the Three Primes, fasting is judged by one’s abstention from taking life.

**Sixth, build bridges, repair roads, dig wells, clear channels, promote benefit, eliminate harm, encourage virtue, resolve doubts, mediate disputes, and end conflicts—all are acts of convenience.**
For the wealthy and powerful, such deeds reach many, ensuring abundant rewards, augmented fortune and longevity, and blessings for descendants. For Daoist practitioners, they fulfill both merit and practice, naturally attracting a teacher and achieving enlightenment. Even those of modest means who act thus perform a difficult task.

As the Reclusive Perfected One once said: "Of old, those who performed meritorious deeds could save a ruined world. The wealthy find it easy to do good, while the poor struggle to follow suit. Yet those who act from a place of difficulty earn merit a hundredfold greater than the wealthy."

**Mirror for Preserving Life in Newly Recovered Cases of Febrile Disease and Heat-Induced Convulsions**
*Recorded by the Preserver of Vitality, Daoist of Ningchuan*

**Taboos for Epidemics**
The *Yellow Emperor’s Inner Canon* asks: "After recovering from febrile disease, why do some suffer relapses?"
Qibo replies: "Eating meat causes recurrence; overeating leads to lingering illness. Lingering illness arises when, despite intense heat, one forces food, allowing heat to lodge within. When grain qi interacts with it, the two heats combine, causing relapse—termed *food relapse*."
Wang Qixuan explains: "When residual heat remains, it spreads throughout the body. *Recurrence* means the illness returns."
After recovering from heat disease, if blood and qi have not stabilized and residual heat persists, premature exertion causes *overstrain relapse*.

Zhang Zhongjing’s *Treatise on Cold Damage* and Cheng Wuji’s commentary state: "If a man has recently recovered but not fully, and a woman lies with him, it is called *yang exchange*. If a woman has recently recovered but not fully, and a man lies with her, it is called *yin exchange*. The interaction of yin and yang stirs residual toxins, which infect like an exchange."
*Sexual relapse* refers to self-induced arousal; it is also called *female overstrain relapse*. Internal depletion of true qi and external stirring of pathogenic heat leave true qi deficient and evil qi flourishing—rendering it incurable. The late Gu Zixian, though recovered, did not heed Hua Tuo’s warnings. On his deathbed, his tongue protruded several inches—a cautionary tale.

**External Causes of Overstrain Relapse**
- Combing hair too early invites head wind.
- Washing the face too early causes head heat.
- Washing the feet too early leads to foot numbness.
- Bathing too early induces fever and dizziness.
- Anger breeds stagnation.
- Long journeys weaken the legs, causing flaccid wind.
- Overexertion leads to hemiplegia.
- Anxiety depletes qi.
- Rising too early or straining the mind and body risks relapse.

**Internal Causes of Food Relapse**
- Eating mutton causes wheezing, suffocation, and death.
- Eating sheep’s heart or lungs risks fatal relapse.
- Eating sheep’s blood or liver causes severe diarrhea.
- Eating beef leads to intractable dysentery.
- Eating sheep or pig intestines causes chronic illness.
- Eating horse meat is lethal.
- Eating poultry too soon is lethal.

**Internal Causes of Food Relapse (Continued)**
- Eating beef liver causes unceasing bloody diarrhea.
- Eating dog meat induces jaundice and certain death.
- Eating roasted meat leads to wasting-thirst.
- Consuming bone broth causes fever and bone steaming.
- Eating rabbit meat harms the heart.
- Eating yellow cattle meat forms intractable abdominal masses.
- Eating chicken meat breeds parasitic illnesses.
- Eating carp risks relapse.
- Eating eel induces vomiting and dysentery.
- Eating fish preserved in brine causes jaundice.
- Eating goose meat triggers cholera.
- Eating blood clams is lethal.
- Eating damp noodles induces tidal fever.
- Eating cucumbers or snake gourds risks fatal relapse.
- Eating eggplant causes malaria.
- Eating white hyacinth beans obstructs the chest with cold qi.
- Eating mallow harms the eyes.
- Eating raw vegetables aggravates heart illness, leading to death and irreversible pallor.

**Other Causes of Relapse**
- Drinking wine too soon induces manic delirium.
- Drinking clear liquor causes edema.
- After recovering from an epidemic with a recent sweat, drinking cold water damages the pericardium, leaving one debilitated and unrecovered.

**Sun Zhenren’s Prescriptions and Discourse:**
After recovering from a febrile illness or major ailment, consuming pork, sheep’s blood, fatty fish, or greasy foods will invariably cause severe diarrhea—an affliction beyond medical remedy, leading to certain death. If one eats pastries, glutinous millet, raw fish, roasted meats, malt sugar, preserved crabs, dried meats, jujubes, chestnuts, or other fruits such as peaches, apricots, plums, and cherries—along with any hard, indigestible foods—the weakened stomach qi will fail to digest them. Purgative medicines must then be administered, but excessive diarrhea will be uncontrollable; without purgation, death is inevitable. Even if purged, recovery remains precarious, and all cases are difficult to save.

Within a hundred days of convalescence, when qi and strength have not yet fully returned, engaging in sexual activity is fatal. Even the robust must abstain for sixty days. After recovery, one should only consume thin rice porridge or gruel, eating sparingly to maintain slight hunger. Avoid satiety, and refrain from all other foods—even if cravings arise, do not indulge them.

For post-illness thirst, *Tianshui Powder* is recommended. Watermelon and Asian pears may quench thirst and dispel residual heat.

Having practiced medicine for over forty years and treated countless patients, I invariably provide these prohibitions and dietary restrictions to those recovering from febrile illnesses, thereby preventing relapse.

Now I observe that among the vulgar and ignorant, some rely on their innate robust constitution, while others suffer only mild afflictions. Though they may fortuitously recover without relapse, they take this as the norm and are misled by the masses. Little do they know that one’s endowment of qi waxes and wanes, and the severity of illness varies—yet they recklessly generalize, and thus countless perish needlessly. There are also mothers who dote on their children, or wives who cherish their husbands, and when they beg for food, these women secretly indulge them. They disregard the gravity of life and death, valuing only the fleeting pleasure of the palate—only to bring harm upon those they love.

Alas, such truths may be shared with the discerning, but are difficult to convey to the common folk. Thus, the wise must exercise utmost caution. Having distilled the wisdom of sages and worthies from their collected works, I have compiled these prohibitions and dietary laws, entitling them *The Mirror for Preserving Life*.

For infants with smallpox or measles, the following ten perils must also be avoided during the "silkworm month":
- The foul odor of armpit fox-musk
- The noxious vapors of ditches and filthy drains
- The turbid, lustful qi of the bedchamber (especially after recent intercourse)
- The menstrual qi of women, along with all manner of bloody, rank odors
- The fumes of alcohol and the stench of meat or fish (inhaling the breath of a drunkard may drive pox toxins inward; if the child drinks wine, the toxins will erupt outward)
- The fumes of sulfur-based mosquito repellents and other toxic substances (if one with red eyes is exposed, the pain will be severe and recovery difficult)
- The restless, impure qi of musk (inhaling musk may draw pox toxins inward)
- The steam and dampness of epidemic sweat (keep coriander nearby on all sides to counteract its effects)
- The acrid smoke of burning hair, fish bones, or other foul odors, as well as wood smoke entering the mouth and nose
- The pungent vapors of onions, garlic, leeks, and chives, along with the greasy fumes of frying oil

The above prohibitions are drawn from *The Complete Collection for Infant Care*; none may be violated, lest complications arise—this I have witnessed firsthand.

Some may argue that rural children, left to their natural state, suffer no ill effects from such transgressions. Yet this overlooks the distinction between noble and base, and the differences in innate endowment.

**Coriander Wine** is used to promote the eruption of smallpox in children. Take three liang of finely chopped coriander, steep it in two large cups of wine, and bring to a boil. Immediately cover to trap the vapors, then allow to cool. Strain and lightly spray the child’s nape, back, chest, abdomen, and feet—avoiding the head and face. Place the leftover coriander in a pouch and hang it in the bed canopy. The remaining wine may be consumed by the wet nurse.

*The Records of the Grand Historian* states: There are six conditions under which illness cannot be cured. The first is arrogance and self-indulgence, refusing to heed reason.

The six conditions under which illness cannot be cured are as follows: The second is valuing wealth over life; the third is failing to regulate clothing and diet; the fourth is when both yin and yang are depleted and the visceral qi is insufficient; the fifth is when the body is too weak to take medicine; the sixth is trusting shamans over physicians.

**Liu Hejian’s Poem on Nursing Infants**
To raise the young requires care and vigilance,
Never indulge or neglect their needs.
Too much milk will harm the stomach,
Excess food will clog the spleen.
Thick quilts bring no benefit,
Light clothing is just right.
Let them see the sun often, free from drafts,
And follow the seasons in warmth and chill.

**Prescriptions for Eye Ailments**
*General Formula for Dispersing, Deficiency, and Excess*
For detoxification, add:
- Mulberry bark (*Sangshu*): 2 liang
- Cimicifuga (*Shengma*): 2 liang
- Red peony (*Chishaoyao*): 3 liang
- Sichuan lovage (*Chuanxiong*): 2 liang
- Bupleurum (*Chaihu*): 3 liang (remove the nodes)
- Kudzu (*Gange*): 3 liang
- Scrophularia (*Xuanshen*): 1 liang (remove the galls)
- Ligusticum (*Fuxiong*): 1 liang
- Scutellaria (*Huangqin*): ½ liang
- Schizonepeta (*Jingjie*): ½ liang
- Licorice (*Gancao*): 1 liang
- White atractylodes (*Baizhu*): ½ liang
- Gardenia (*Shanzhizi*): ½ liang
- Red poria (*Chifuling*): 1 liang
- Cassia seed (*Jumingshi*): use sparingly
Boil in plain water and take.

*Qianghuo Powder for Heat*
- Ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*): 2 liang
- Notopterygium (*Qianghuo*): 1 liang
- Red peony (*Chishaoyao*): 3 liang
- Angelica (*Baizhi*): 1 liang
- Sichuan lovage (*Chuanxiong*): 2 liang
- Bupleurum (*Chaihu*): 1 liang
- Alisma (*Zexie*): ½ liang
- Stephania (*Fangji*): ½ liang
- Licorice (*Gancao*): 1 liang
- Schizonepeta (*Jingjie*): 1 liang
- White poria (*Baifuling*): 2 liang
- Chrysanthemum (*Juhua*): 1 liang
- Asarum (*Xixin*): ½ liang (remove the leaves)
- White atractylodes (*Baizhu*): 1 liang

*Purgative Formula*
- Red peony (*Chishaoyao*)
- Scutellaria (*Huangqin*)
- Bitter orange (*Zhike*)
- Schizonepeta (*Jingjie*)
Boil equal parts until done, then steep with rhubarb (*Dahuang*) and mirabilite (*Poxia*). Take at the fifth watch (before dawn).

*For all accumulations of heat with swelling and pain.*

*Danggui Powder, suitable for the old and young, weak and strong*
- Chinese angelica (*Danggui*): 2 liang (soaked and washed in wine)
- Sichuan lovage (*Chuanxiong*): 2 liang
- Red peony (*Chishaoyao*): 3 liang
- Prepared rehmannia (*Shudihuang*): 1 liang (washed in wine)
- Schizonepeta (*Jingjie*): ½ liang
- Licorice (*Gancao*): ½ liang
- Ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*): 1 liang
- Angelica (*Baizhi*): 1 liang
Boil in plain water and take.

*Jili Pill for Removing All Obstructions and Films*
- Abalone shell (*Shijueming*)
- Sichuan lovage (*Chuanxiong*)
- Angelica (*Baizhi*)
- Ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*)
- Scouring rush (*Muzei*)
- Gypsum (*Shigao*)
- Palmleaf raspberry (*Fupenzi*)
- Paper mulberry fruit (*Chushizi*, remove the husk, use rice)
- Cicada molting (*Chantui*)
- Vitex fruit (*Manjingzi*)
- Celosia seed (*Qingxiangzi*)
- Plantago seed (*Cheqianzi*)
- Asarum (*Xixin*)
- Chrysanthemum (*Juhua*)
- Inula flower (*Xuanfuhua*)
- Buddleia flower (*Mimenghua*)
- Gentian (*Longdan*)
Grind equal parts, form into honey pills. For deficiency, take with a decoction of *Guan* herbs; for excess, take with a decoction of imperata root (*Maogen*) and sugarcane; for pearl-like obstructions, take with a decoction of pig’s liver; for dense films, take with a decoction of twenty-four ingredients. In severe cases, add persimmon calyx (*Baishi*), mulberry bark (*Sangbaipi*), imperata root (*Maogen*), and sugarcane, and boil for the decoction.

*Divine Response Returning Light Powder for Obstructive Films, Red Eyes, and Pterygium*
- Scouring rush (*Muzei*)
- Angelica (*Baizhi*)
- Licorice (*Gancao*)

Grind into powder. Take 1 qian after meals, mixed with tea or wine.

*For bruised, blood-swollen eyelids*
- Rhubarb (*Dahuang*)

Grind into powder, mix with rehmannia juice, place on paper, and apply to the affected area.

*For bruises with blood invading the eye*
- Peach branches (*Taozhi*)
- Willow branches (*Liuzhi*)
- Rehmannia (*Shengdihuang*)
Pound the herbs with pork and apply to the eyelids.

*For heat accumulation in the heart with red veins descending into the pupil*
Use any amount of scrophularia (*Xuanshen*) powder. Cook pig’s liver in rice-washing water, dip in the powder, chew finely, and swallow with the broth.

*For cold tears from the eyes*, use the *Four Agents Decoction* to tonify the liver, adding alisma (*Zexie*) and ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*). For deficiency, use this formula. For excess, use:
- Alisma (*Zexie*)
- Atractylodes (*Cangzhu*)
- White tribulus (*Baijili*)
- Ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*)
- Notopterygium (*Qianghuo*)
- Sichuan lovage (*Chuanxiong*)
- Licorice (*Gancao*)
Grind into powder and take with rice-washing water.

*For eye pain with red blood wheels*, purge the heart with:
- Gentian (*Longdancao*)
- Asarum (*Xixin*)
- Gardenia (*Shanzhizi*)
- Rhubarb (*Dahuang*)
- Licorice (*Gancao*)
- Black soybeans (*Wudou*)
Boil in water and take.

*For redness encroaching on the white of the eye*, purge the liver with:
- Apricot kernel (*Xingren*, remove the skin)
- Knotgrass (*Bianxu*)
- Mulberry bark (*Sangbaipi*)
Take warm.

*Qingshen Powder for Wind in the Kidney Viscera Attacking the Eyes*
- White mustard flower (*Baixianhua*)
- Ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*)
- Notopterygium (*Qianghuo*)
- Phellodendron (*Huangbo*)
Grind into powder and take with warm wine.

*For redness in both the blood and water wheels of the eye*, use the *Rehmannia Pill* to tonify the kidneys, the *Red Poria Pill*, and the *Fennel Pill*. Combine the three, form into twenty pills, and take with a *Guan* decoction or salted wine.

*Rehmannia Pill*
- Rehmannia (*Shengdihuang*, baked)
- Scutellaria (*Huangqin*)
- Cassia seed (*Jumingshi*, stir-fried)
Form into honey pills.

*For squinting eyes*, combine the *Xiaofeng Powder* and *Heishen Powder*, and take with tea.

*For festering eyelid margins due to wind*
Use any amount of calamine (*Luganshi*). Calcine until red, quench seven times in boy’s urine, grind with milk, and levigate with water to remove sediment. Decoct a strong decoction of coptis (*Huanglian*), Chinese angelica (*Danggui*), peony (*Shaoyao*), schizonepeta (*Jingjie*), ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*), mint (*Bohe*), and asarum (*Xixin*). Place gall insects inside the decoction, and grind repeatedly in a mortar until dry. Store in a porcelain jar. Before use, wash the eyes with hot tea, then apply the medicine. It will take effect immediately.

*Eye Drops*
- Red peony (*Chishaoyao*)
- Cattail pollen (*Puhuang*)
- Hibiscus (*Furong*)
Grind evenly into powder. For pearl-like obstructions, mix with snail slime and ginger juice.

For chronic, persistent eye pain, use only tea infusion; for severe pain, add angelica dahurica (*Baizhi*), arisaema (*Nanxing*), *wumingyi*, and *baiyuanchou*. If the condition fails to resolve over time, add raw Sichuan aconite (*Sheng Chuanwu*).

*To grind away long-standing obstructions in the aged and weak:*
- Cicada slough (*Chantui*): 2 *qian*
- Sichuan lovage (*Chuanxiong*): 2 *qian*

Grind the above into powder, refine with honey into pills the size of a bullet. Take one pill each time, chewed with scallion tea after meals.

**Supplementing the Liver and Enhancing Clarity Pill**
- Antelope horn (*Lingyangjiao*): 1 *liang*
- Fresh rehmannia (*Shengdihuang*): 1 *liang*
- Prepared rehmannia (*Shudihuang*): 1 *liang*
- Cistanche (*Roucongrong*): 1 *liang*
- Lycium fruit (*Gouqizi*): 1 *liang*
- Ledebouriella (*Fangfeng*): 1 *liang*
- Cassia seed (*Caojueming*): 1 *liang*

- Chrysanthemum (*Ganjuhua*): 1 *liang*
- Notopterygium (*Qianghuo*): 1 *liang*
- Chinese angelica (*Danggui*): 1 *liang*
- Sheep liver (*Yangzigan*): 4 *liang* (boiled and dried)

Grind into powder, form into honey pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take thirty pills per dose.

Generally, the liver governs the eyes; the liver receives blood and thus enables vision. If blood is weak, the liver’s *qi* lacks nourishment, and if the liver’s *qi* is not flourishing, the gallbladder’s fluid cannot ascend. This leads to blurred vision, weak eyesight, and unclear perception in children. This formula greatly supplements liver blood, enriches gallbladder fluid, and resolves hidden obstructions in the eyes.

Take on an empty stomach with salted water to guide the formula downward. At midday, take with tea to clear the head and eyes. Before sleep, take with wine to nourish liver blood. For those who do not drink, take with a decoction of ginseng and Chinese angelica. Prolonged use yields excellent results.

**For Pterygium**
In the twelfth lunar month, use a male pig’s gallbladder, fill with *mayaxiao* (sodium sulfate), and dry in the wind. Grind into powder, add *naozi* (borneol) and musk, and apply.

**Processed Refined Mirabilite**
Effective for hot eyes and red eyes.
Take one yellow ox gallbladder, fill with 2 *qian* of pure mirabilite and 1 *qian* of coptis, and hang in the wind. Daily, use a duck feather to brush the mirabilite from the outside of the gallbladder until exhausted. Store in an earthenware jar. Use as usual for application.

**For Smallpox in Children**
Do not purge residual toxin. Only use mung bean skin and *gujingcao* (pipewort) in formulas. Avoid all other foods; regularly eating snails is beneficial.

**For Smallpox Affecting the Eyes**
Take white persimmon.

**Next Method:**
Take a piece of processed mugwort (*Artemisia argyi*) the size of a chicken egg, wrap it around one grain each of cinnabar (*zhusha*), frankincense (*ruxiang*), and arsenic (*pi*), all ground finely to the size of soybeans. Place these inside the mugwort, ignite to produce smoke, and fumigate the medicine in the bowl until the mugwort is fully consumed. Remove and grind finely; use a dose the size of a millet grain to apply to the eye.

**Frequent Eye-Washing Formula**
For all types of wind-heat, heart-heat, wind-toxin erosion, redness, roughness, itching, pain, obstructions, nebulae, and blood-wind conditions in women.
- *Wubeizi* (gallnut), sifted to remove impurities
- *Manjingzi* (vitex fruit), remove white skin, wash with hot water

Grind into powder. For each dose of 2 *qian*, place in a sand pot with half a cup of water and 30–50 copper coins. Seal the mouth with paper, heat over fire for a long time, then pierce a small hole in the paper to allow steam to fumigate the eyes. When the temperature is tolerable, pour out the clear liquid and wash the eyes while warm; stop when cool. Reheat and wash again.

**Another Eye-Washing Formula**
- *Tongqing* (verdigris): 0.5 *liang*
- *Baiyuntu* (white clay): 1 *liang*
- *Wubeizi* (gallnut): 1.5 *qian*

Grind together into powder, steep in hot water, and wash the eyes while warm with eyes closed. Do not let the solution enter the eyes; stop when cool, then reheat and wash again. Effective for all cases of erosive canthus.

**Tea-Blended Powder**
For men and women suffering from all types of wind-swelling, itching, pain, nebulae, erosive canthus, *qi*-induced tearing, and blurred vision.
- *Chuanxiong* (Sichuan lovage rhizome)

- Peppermint (*Boheye*)

Grind into powder. Take 2 *qian* per dose with tea.

**For All Heat-Induced Eye Conditions**
First, take 4 *liang* of *Huanglian* (coptis), slice, and decoct into a thick paste. Then, take one large sweet melon, cut open the top, scoop out the seeds, and layer with fresh peppermint and *mayaxiao* (sodium sulfate) until the melon is full. Replace the top and hang in a windy place for 3–4 days. The *xiaoshao* will crystallize on the melon’s skin; brush it off daily with a goose feather and mix evenly with the coptis paste. Store in a white vessel and apply to hot eyes.

**Plaster for Red, Hot Eyes**

- *Jingjie* (schizonepeta): 0.5 *liang*

- Rhubarb (*Dahuang*): 0.5 *liang*

Grind into powder, mix with honey water, and apply to the *taiyang* acupoints to reduce heat and blood.

**Purple Gold Pill**
A secret formula for eye conditions.
- *Chuanxiong* (Sichuan lovage rhizome): 1.5 *liang*
- *Danggui* (Chinese angelica): 1.5 *liang*
- *Chushi* (paper mulberry fruit): 0.5 *liang*
- Peppermint (*Bohe*): 0.5 *liang*
- Trichosanthes root (*Gualougen*): 6 *qian*

Soak the above four ingredients in licorice juice, then bake dry.

Grind the thirteen ingredients into fine powder, refine with honey, and form into pills weighing 1 *qian* each. Take with the appropriate adjuvant:
- For dim, bluish nebulae: with *Danggui* wine
- For *qi*-induced obstructions: with *Muxiang* (costus root) decoction
- For women’s blood dizziness: with *Danggui* and peppermint decoction

One person, after drinking hot wine, suffered from eye problems for three years, unable to distinguish roads; after taking this medicine for twenty-five days, improvement was seen. Another, whose vision was impaired by *qi* for eight years, regained clarity after forty days, with full recovery in sixty days. Yet another, who lost sight for four years after a mother’s death, regained vision after fifty days, returning to former clarity.

For all types of eye diseases, nebulae, obstructions, and dimness, highly effective.

- For those with clouded vision: with rice-washing water
