Avoid raw, fishy, alcoholic, and damp foods. This medicine has proven repeatedly effective.

**For Hot Wind Eyes**
Take an unspecified quantity of *Dongqingzi* (wintergreen fruit), crush to extract juice, and simmer into a paste. Filter thoroughly, store in a porcelain jar, and bury underground for seven days to remove fire toxin. Use to apply to hot eyes.

**Another Formula**
Take 4 *liang* each of *Huanglian* (coptis) and *Poxiao* (sodium sulfate), decoct with water into a paste, and apply to hot eyes.

**Another Formula**
Take carp gallbladder juice while warm and apply to the eyes.

**Excellent Formula for Erosive Canthus**
First wash with *Wubeizi* (gallnut) and *Manjingzi* (vitex fruit). Then take 2 *liang* of *Luganshi* (calamine), calcine in fire, and quench seven or eight times with coptis juice and boys’ urine. Grind finely, then add 5 *qian* of *Tongqing* (verdigris), 1 *qian* of *Pengsha* (borax), a small amount of musk (*Shexiang*), and 0.5 *qian* of *Yaxiao* (sodium sulfate). Grind into fine powder and apply to the canthus.

**For Infants Under One Year Old with Red Eyes**
Grind *Huanglian* (coptis) into powder, mix with tea, and apply to the palms and soles; this will cure the condition. If swelling and pain make opening the eyes difficult, add *Jianghuang* (turmeric), *Zaojiao* (Chinese honey locust), and *Poxiao* (sodium sulfate) to the powder, and apply to the *taiyang* acupoints and palms/soles. Adding crushed scallions enhances the effect.

*End of Scroll Eleven of the Immortal’s Transmitted External Medicine Secret Formulas*

**Appendix: On Exerting Effort to Practice Convenience**

In this world, convenience is foremost; where strength suffices, act without delay—regret follows hesitation.

For those of wealth, nobility, and power, the sway of fortune and misfortune over others is effortless. When facing matters, let convenience guide the heart: granting one measure of leniency bestows one measure of blessing upon others. Further, exert oneself in good deeds, practicing every form of convenience without pause. People will revere such virtue as that of sages who benefit all under heaven—no merit surpasses this.

**1. Selling Grain at Fair Prices is the Greatest Convenience.**
The Celestial Master Han Ancestor taught that the foremost merit lies in saving others. Those with wealth, upon harvest, should broadly purchase and store grain, or if possessing fields, accumulate reserves. When scarcity arises, sell at the original price—no loss to oneself, yet immense benefit to others. Formerly, Huang Chengshi of Chengdu practiced this and was honored by the Purple Mansion Perfected Lord, Minister Zhang. He ascended to the immortal registers and enjoyed prosperity for generations. Alternatively, selling at a reduced price during lean times is even more commendable.

**2. Relieving Illness is a Great Convenience.**
If one can devoutly prepare and distribute the *Ruyi Elixir* of the Perfected Lord Xu, it cures myriad ailments, especially swift in treating epidemics. Other efficacious medicines for distribution are also excellent, as is printing and disseminating proven remedies.

**3. In summer, distribute water; in winter, provide clothing for the elderly and infirm. Show compassion to widows, orphans, the childless, and the solitary. Foster abandoned children. Supply coffins to the unburied. Relieve those in urgent distress or poverty as circumstances allow.**

**4. Deliverance of the Deceased is of Small Cost but Great Merit.**
Master Ge the Immortal and Perfected Lord Sa attained transcendence through this, and all past immortals and masters have emphasized it. If one consistently performs sacrificial refinement, blessings extend to the departed. Even occasional fasting and food offerings confer no small benefit.

Enlightened individuals and upright scholars, through exhaustive study and inquiry, awaken to the illusory nature of life and destiny and master the Dao of reversing water and fire. Not only do they transcend the mundane, but they also deliver the departed from the netherworld. The accumulation of deeds and merits begins here—one must seek a master’s guidance to avoid squandering effort.

**5. The Suffering of Living Beings is Shared with Humans.**
Where possible, refrain from killing. Treat insects, birds, and beasts with equal compassion. The scriptures prescribe fasting and releasing life on the Three Officials’ days, for the Three Primes’ assessments deem all fasting as abstention from taking life.

**6. Repairing bridges, mending roads, digging wells, clearing channels, promoting benefit, eliminating harm, exhorting goodness, resolving doubts, mediating disputes—all are acts of convenience.**

For the wealthy who practice such conveniences, their reach is vast, and their recompense abundant. Blessings and longevity increase, and their families enjoy lasting felicity. For Dao cultivators, this ensures both merit and practice are fulfilled, naturally encountering masters and attaining the Dao. For those of modest means, such deeds are especially difficult. As the Pure Nourishment Perfected One once said: *"Of old, those who performed meritorious deeds could succor the world’s destitute. The wealthy find it easy to act, while the poor find it hard to emulate. Yet those who act where emulation is difficult achieve merit a hundredfold greater than the wealthy."*

---

**Mirror for Preserving Life in Newly Recovered Cases of Cold Damage, Febrile Diseases, and Convulsions**
*Recorded by Ningchuan, the Daoist of Preserving Nurturance*

**Epidemics share the same prohibitions.** The *Yellow Emperor’s Inner Canon* asks: *"After recovering from cold damage or febrile illness, why do some symptoms linger?"*
Qibo replied: *"Eating meat causes relapse; overeating causes lingering illness. Lingering occurs when, despite intense heat, one forces food, allowing heat to hide and combine with grain qi. The two heats merge, causing residual symptoms—termed *food relapse*."*
Wang Qixuan explained: *"When heat qi is not fully expelled, it lingers and afflicts the body. Relapse means falling ill again."*

**Labor Relapse**
After recent recovery from febrile illness, blood and qi are not yet restored, and residual heat remains. Premature exertion causes *labor relapse*.

**Zhang Zhongjing’s Discussion on Yin-Yang Exchange in Cold Damage (Annotated by Cheng Wuji):**
If a man recently recovered but not fully restored engages in intercourse with a woman, the illness is called *yang exchange*. If a woman in the same state engages with a man, it is called *yin exchange*. The mutual stimulation of yin and yang, along with residual toxin transmission, resembles an exchange.

**Sexual Relapse**
This refers to self-induced lust, also called *female labor relapse*. It depletes true qi internally and stirs pathogenic heat externally. With genuine deficiency and pathogenic excess, it becomes untreatable. Formerly, Gu Zixian, though recovered, did not heed Hua Fu’s cautions. Before death, his tongue protruded several inches—a warning not to be ignored.

**External Injuries from Labor Relapse**
- Combing hair too early inevitably causes head wind.
- Washing the face too early leads to head dampness and heat.
- Washing the feet too early results in foot numbness.
- Bathing too early induces fever and stupor.
- Agitation and anger cause abdominal masses.
- Long journeys lead to weak, flaccid legs.
- Overexertion causes hemiplegia.
- Anxiety depletes qi.
- Rising too early or straining the mind and body risks relapse.

**Internal Injuries from Food Relapse**
- Eating mutton causes relapse with fatal wheezing.
- Eating sheep’s heart or lungs risks fatal relapse.
- Eating sheep’s blood or liver causes severe diarrhea.
- Eating beef leads to intractable dysentery.
- Eating sheep or pig intestines causes chronic illness.
- Eating horse meat is lethal.
- Eating poultry too soon is lethal.
- Eating beef liver causes unstoppable bloody diarrhea.
- Eating dog meat induces fatal jaundice.
- Eating roasted meat causes wasting-thirst.
- Eating bone broth induces fever and bone steaming.
- Eating rabbit meat causes heart disease.
- Eating yellow beef causes unbreakable abdominal masses.
- Eating chicken causes parasitic diseases.
- Eating carp causes relapse.
- Eating eel induces vomiting and dysentery.
- Eating preserved fish causes jaundice.
- Eating goose meat causes cholera.

Eating ark clams is lethal. Eating damp noodles induces damp-heat. Eating cucumbers or angled luffa causes fatal relapse. Eating eggplant induces malaria. Eating white hyacinth beans obstructs cold qi in the chest. Eating mallow causes blindness. Eating raw vegetables leads to fatal heart disease and irreversible complexion. Drinking wine too soon induces manic agitation. Drinking white liquor causes edema.

During epidemic outbreaks, after sweating resolves the illness, drinking cold water harms the pericardium, leaving one debilitated and unrecovered. Master Sun’s *Treatise on Formulas* states: After recovering from febrile diseases or major illnesses, eating pork, sheep’s blood, fatty fish, or greasy foods will inevitably cause severe diarrhea, which physicians cannot cure and is fatal. Consuming pastries, glutinous millet, raw fish, roasted meats, malt sugar, crab, dried meats, preserved fruits, jujubes, chestnuts, peaches, apricots, plums, or other hard-to-digest foods—while the stomach qi remains weak and unable to transform them—will necessitate purgative medicine. Uncontrollable diarrhea may follow, and without purgation, death is certain. Even with purgation, recovery is perilous and difficult to save.

Before one hundred days have passed after recovery, when qi and strength have not yet returned, engaging in sexual activity is lethal; even the robust must abstain for sixty days. After recovery, one should only consume thin rice porridge, eating sparingly to maintain hunger and carefully avoiding satiety. No other foods should be eaten, even if craved. For thirst after sourness, one may take *Tianshui Powder*, or consume watermelon or water pears to quench thirst and dispel residual heat.

Having practiced medicine for over forty years and treated many patients, I invariably provide these prohibitions and dietary rules to those recovering from febrile illnesses, to prevent relapse.

Herein I observe the ignorant and base among the common folk, who, relying on their innate robust constitutions or having suffered only mild afflictions, deem themselves fortunate to escape relapse and thus take such peril lightly, swayed by the misguided counsel of the multitude. They fail to grasp that one’s endowment of qi may wax or wane, that the severity of illness varies, and that reckless disregard—treating all cases alike—has led countless to their deaths.

Some mothers, out of love for their children, or wives for their husbands, secretly indulge their cravings for food, valuing fleeting gustatory pleasure over life itself, thereby unwittingly hastening harm. Alas, such truths are fit to share with the discerning, yet difficult to impress upon the vulgar—thus must the wise exercise utmost caution.

Having distilled the wisdom of sages and worthies from their collected works, I have compiled these prohibitions and dietary rules, entitling them *The Mirror for Preserving Life*. The following must also be strictly avoided in cases of infantile pox and eruptive rashes, as well as during the ten perilous months of pregnancy:

- The foul odor of fox-like armpit secretions
- The noxious vapors of ditches and filthy channels
- The turbid, lascivious qi of the bedchamber (especially after recent intercourse)
- The menstrual qi and all manner of bloody, rank odors
- The fumes of alcohol and the stench of meat or fish (inhaling the breath of a drunkard may drive pox toxin inward; if the child drinks wine, the toxin erupts outward)
- The acrid vapors of sulfur-based mosquito repellents and other toxic substances (contact with these may cause red, painful eyes that resist healing)
- The restless, impure qi of musk (inhaling it may draw pox toxin inward)
- The steam and dampness of epidemic sweat (keep coriander nearby to counteract its miasma)
- The stench of singed hair, fish bones, or other foul odors, as well as woodsmoke entering the mouth or nose
- The pungent qi of onions, garlic, and leeks
- The greasy fumes of frying oil

The above prohibitions are drawn from *The Complete Compendium for Infants* and must not be violated, lest complications arise—this I have witnessed firsthand.

Some argue that peasant children, left to nature’s course, suffer no ill effects from such transgressions, attributing this to differences in social station and innate endowment. Yet this is not so.

For infantile pox desiring outward expression, prepare *Coriander Wine*: finely chop three liang of coriander, steep in two large cups of wine, and bring to a boil. Cover tightly to trap the vapors, then cool and strain. Lightly spray the child’s nape, back, chest, abdomen, and feet, avoiding the face and head. Place the lees in a pouch and hang it within the bed-curtains; the nursing mother may consume the remaining decoction.

The *Records of the Historian* states: "There are six conditions that render illness incurable. The first is arrogance and self-indulgence, refusing to heed reason..."

Those who value wealth over life are the second incurable case; those unable to regulate clothing and diet are the third; those with concurrent depletion of yin and yang and visceral qi are the fourth; those too frail to take medicine are the fifth; and those who trust shamans but not physicians are the sixth.

*Liu Hejian’s Poem on Nursing Infants*
To raise the young requires care and protection,
Attend to them without indulgence or neglect.
Excess milk will harm the stomach,
Stagnant food will injure the spleen.
Thick quilts bring no benefit,
Light clothing is most suitable.
Expose them often to sunlight, free from drafts,
And follow the seasons in cold and heat.

*Various Remedies for Eye Diseases*
**General Formula for Dispersing, Deficiency, and Excess**
For detoxification, add:
- 2 liang of *Sanguisorba* (Sang tree) *shengma*
- 3 liang of *Paeonia lactiflora* *chishaoyao*
- 2 liang of *Ligusticum chuanxiong*
- 3 liang of *Bupleurum* *chaihu* (remove the nodes)
- 3 liang of *Pueraria* *gan’ge*
- 1 liang of *Scrophularia* *xuanshen* (remove the galls)
- 1 liang of *Ligusticum sinense* *fuxiong*
- ½ liang of *Scutellaria* *huangqin*
- ½ liang of *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*
- 1 liang of *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*
- ½ liang of *Atractylodes* *baizhu*
- ½ liang of *Gardenia* *shanzhizi*
- 1 liang of *Poria* *fuling*
- A small amount of *Cassia obtusifolia* *caojue ming*
Boil in plain water and take.

**Qianghuo Powder for Heat**
- 2 liang of *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*
- 1 liang of *Notopterygium* *qianghuo*
- 3 liang of *Paeonia lactiflora* *chishaoyao*
- 1 liang of *Angelica dahurica* *baizhi*
- 2 liang of *Ligusticum chuanxiong*
- 1 liang of *Bupleurum* *chaihu*
- ½ liang of *Alisma* *zexie*
- ½ liang of *Stephania tetrandra* *fangji*
- 1 liang of *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*
- 1 liang of *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*
- 2 liang of *Poria* *fuling*
- 1 liang of *Chrysanthemum* *juhua*
- ½ liang of *Asarum* *xixin* (remove the leaves)
- 1 liang of *Atractylodes* *baizhu*

**Purgative Formula**
- *Paeonia lactiflora* *chishaoyao*
- *Scutellaria* *huangqin*
- *Aurantium* *zhiqiao*
- *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*
Boil the above in equal parts, then steep *Rheum palmatum* *dahuang* and *Mirabilite* *poxiao* in the decoction. Take at the fifth watch (around 3–5 AM).

For all cases of accumulated heat with swelling and pain, use this.

**Danggui Powder, Suitable for All Ages and Conditions**
- 2 liang of *Angelica sinensis* *danggui* (soaked in wine and washed)
- 2 liang of *Ligusticum chuanxiong*
- 3 liang of *Paeonia lactiflora* *chishaoyao*
- 1 liang of *Rehmannia* *shudihuang* (washed in wine)
- ½ liang of *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*
- ½ liang of *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*
- 1 liang of *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*
- 1 liang of *Angelica dahurica* *baizhi*
Boil in plain water and take.

**Jili Pill for Resolving All Obstructions and Films**
- *Haliotis* *shijueming*
- *Ligusticum chuanxiong*
- *Angelica dahurica* *baizhi*
- *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*
- *Equisetum* *muzei*
- *Gypsum* *shigao*
- *Rubus* *fupenzi*
- *Broussonetia* *chushizi* (remove the shell, use the kernel with rice)
- *Cryptotympana* *chantui*
- *Vitex* *manjingzi*
- *Celastrus* *qingxiangzi*
- *Plantago* *cheqianzi*
- *Asarum* *xixin*
- *Chrysanthemum* *juhua*
- *Inula* *xuanfuhua*
- *Buddleja* *mimenghua*
- *Gentiana* *longdan*
Grind equal parts into powder, form into pills with honey. For deficiency, take with a decoction of *Imperata* *maogen* and sugarcane; for severe cases, add *Diospyros* *baishi*, *Morus* *sangbaipi*, *Imperata* *maogen*, and sugarcane decoction. For pearl-like obstructions, take with *Ershiwu Wu Tang* (Twenty-Four Ingredients Decoction); for severe cases, add *white persimmon*, *mulberry root bark*, *Imperata root*, and sugarcane decoction.

**Shenying Huiguang Powder for Obstructive Films, Red Eyes, and Pterygium**
- *Equisetum* *muzei*
- *Angelica dahurica* *baizhi*
- *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*
- *Celastrus* *qingxiangzi*
- *Broussonetia* *chushizi*
- *Cassia obtusifolia* *caojue ming*
- *Notopterygium* *qianghuo*
- *Haliotis* *shijueming*
- *Aconitum* *chuanwu* (soaked)
- *Ampelopsis* *baixianhua*
- *Cryptotympana* *chantui*
Grind into powder. Take 1 qian after meals, mixed with tea or wine.

**Huanjing Pill**
- *Tribulus* *baijili*
- *Alisma* *zexie*
- *Clematis* *weilingxian*
- *Cryptotympana* *chantui*
- *Chrysanthemum* *juhua*
- *Haliotis* *shijueming*
- *Cassia obtusifolia* *caojue ming*
- *Ligusticum chuanxiong*
- *Notopterygium* *qianghuo*
- *Celastrus* *qingxiangzi*
- *Buddleja* *mimenghua*
- *Broussonetia* *chushizi*
Grind equal parts into powder, form into pills with honey.

For cloudy vision, add *raw sesame oil*, *Mentha* *bohe*, *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*, and *Forsythia* *lianqiao* to *Si Wu Tang* (Four Substances Decoction). Boil in water and take after meals.

**For Traumatic Injury with Blood Stasis and Swollen Eyelids**
- *Rheum palmatum* *dahuang*
- *Curcuma longa* *jianghuang*
- *Coptis* *huanglian*
- *Phellodendron* *huangbo*
- *Angelica sinensis* *danggui*
- *Calcium carbonate* *baifan*
- *Ampelopsis* *bailian*
- *Schinus* *wubeizi*
- *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*
- *Mirabilite* *poxiao*
- *Mentha* *bohe*
Grind into powder, mix with *Rehmannia* *shengdihuang* juice, spread on paper, and apply to the affected area.

**For Traumatic Injury with Blood Invading the Eye**
- *Peach twigs*
- *Willow twigs*
- *Rehmannia* *shengdihuang*
Pound the above with pork and apply to the eyelids.

**For Accumulated Heart Heat with Red Vessels Descending into the Pupil**
Grind *Scrophularia* *xuanshen* into powder without limit. Cook pig liver in rice-washing water, dip in the powder, chew finely, and swallow with the juice.

**For Cold Tears from the Eyes, Tonify the Liver with Si Wu Tang**
Add *Alisma* *zexie* and *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*. For deficiency, use this.
For excess, use:
- *Alisma* *zexie*
- *Atractylodes* *cangzhu*
- *Tribulus* *baijili*
- *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*
- *Notopterygium* *qianghuo*
- *Ligusticum chuanxiong*
- *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*
Grind into powder and take with rice-washing water.

**For Eye Pain with Red Blood Wheels, Purge the Heart**
- *Gentiana* *longdancao*
- *Asarum* *xixin*
- *Gardenia* *shanzhizi*
- *Rheum palmatum* *dahuang*
- *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*
- *Black soybeans*
Boil in water and take.

**For Redness Encroaching on the Whites, Purge the Liver with Yinzi Decoction**
- *Prunus armeniaca* *xingren* (remove the skin)
- *Polygonum aviculare* *bianxu*
- *Morus* *sangbaipi*
Take warm.

**Qingshen Powder for Wind in the Kidney Viscera Attacking the Eyes**
- *Ampelopsis* *baixianhua*
- *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*
- *Notopterygium* *qianghuo*
- *Phellodendron* *huangbo*
Grind into powder and take with warm wine.

**For Both Blood and Water Wheels Red, Tonify the Kidney**
Use *Dihuang Pill*, *Chixue Pill*, or *Huixiang Pill*. Combine the three, form into twenty pills, and take with a decoction of *Imperata* or salted wine.

**Dihuang Pill**
- *Rehmannia* *shengdihuang* (baked)
- *Scutellaria* *huangqin*
- *Cassia obtusifolia* *caojue ming* (stir-fried)
Form into pills with honey.

**For Squinting Eyes**
Combine *Xiaofeng Powder* and *Heishen Powder*, take with tea.

**For Blepharitis Marginalis (Burning Eyelid Wind)**
Use *Lu Ganshi* (calamine) without limit. Calcine until red, quench seven times in boy’s urine, grind finely, and levigate with water to remove impurities. Decoct *Coptis* *huanglian*, *Angelica sinensis* *danggui*, *Paeonia lactiflora* *shaoyao*, *Schizonepeta* *jingjie*, *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*, *Mentha* *bohe*, and *Asarum* *xixin* into a thick decoction. Place *wubeizi* insects in the decoction, grind repeatedly in a mortar until dry, and store in a porcelain jar. Before use, wash the eyes with hot tea, then apply the powder—immediate efficacy.

**Eye Drops**
- *Paeonia lactiflora* *chishaoyao*
- *Typha* *puhuang*
- *Hibiscus mutabilis* *furong*
Grind into powder, mix evenly, and blend with *pearl powder*, *oyster shell*, *snail*, and ginger juice.

If chronic pain persists, use only tea infusion; for severe pain, add *Angelica dahurica* *baizhi*, *Arisaema* *nanxing*, *pyrolusite* *wumingyi*, and *Aconitum* *baiyuanchou*. For long-standing cases that fail to resolve, add raw *Aconitum carmichaelii* *shengchuanwu*.

**For Grinding Away Obstructions in Aged or Deficient Patients**
- *Cicada slough* *chantui*: 2 *qian*
- *Ligusticum chuanxiong*: 2 *qian*
- *Antelope horn* *lingyangjiao*: 0.5 *liang*
- *Tribulus terrestris* *baihanhua* (stir-fried, thorns removed): 2 *qian*
- *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao* (stir-fried): 0.5 *qian*
- *Angelica sinensis* *danggui*: 2 *qian*
- *Rehmannia glutinosa* *shudihuang*: 0.5 *qian*
- *Equisetum hyemale* *muzei* (nodes removed): 1 *qian*
- *Prunella vulgaris* *xiakucao*: 0.5 *qian*
- *Haliotis* *shijueming* (calcined): 2 *qian*
- *Gypsum* *shigao* (calcined): 1 *qian*
- *Scrophularia ningpoensis* *xuanshen*: 0.5 *qian*
- *Celastrus orbiculatus* *qingxiangzi*: 1 *qian*

Grind into powder, refine with honey into pills the size of a bullet. Take one pill per dose, chewed and swallowed with scallion tea after meals.

**Fangfeng Powder**
For wind-toxin attacking the eyes, with loss of eyelashes and swollen pain.
- *Saposhnikovia* *fangfeng*
- *Chrysanthemum* *ganjuhua*
- *Coptis* *huanglian*
- *Cassia obtusifolia* *juemingzi*

- *Akebia* *mutong*

Slice and decoct in one cup of water for oral administration.

**Fuling Powder**
For persistent red eyes in the elderly.
- *Poria* *fuling*: 1 *liang*
- *Panax ginseng* *renshen*: 1 *liang*
- *Paeonia lactiflora* *chishaoyao*: 1 *liang*
- *Gardenia jasminoides* *shanzhizi*: 1 *liang*
- *Glycyrrhiza* *gancao*: 1 *liang*
- *Perilla* *zisuye*: 1 *liang*
- *Ophiopogon japonicus* *maimendong*: 1 *liang*
- *Dianthus superbus* *qumai*: 1 *liang*
- *Forsythia* *lianqiao*: 2 *liang*

Slice and decoct in water for oral administration.

**For Women’s Blood-Wind Headache**
*Cao wu* (processed *Aconitum*) and *shanzhizi* (*Gardenia*)—grind into powder, mix with natural onion juice, and apply to the temples and above the brows. Avoid contact with the eyes. After application, avoid wind. Apply only to areas of headache.

**Liver-Nourishing Bright-Vision Pill**
- *Lingyangjiao* (*Saiga antelope horn*): 1 *liang*
- *Sheng dihuang* (*Rehmannia*, raw): 1 *liang*
- *Shu dihuang* (*Rehmannia*, prepared): 1 *liang*
- *Rou cong rong* (*Cistanche*): 1 *liang*
- *Gouqizi* (*Lycium* berries): 1 *liang*
- *Fangfeng* (*Saposhnikovia*): 1 *liang*
- *Cao jueming* (*Cassia obtusifolia*): 1 *liang*
- *Chushizi* (*Broussonetia* fruit): 0.5 *liang*
- *Ganjuhua* (*Chrysanthemum*): 1 *liang*
- *Qianghuo* (*Notopterygium*): 1 *liang*
- *Danggui* (*Angelica sinensis*): 1 *liang*
- *Yang zigan* (*sheep’s liver*): 4 *liang* (boiled and dried)

Grind into powder, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of *wutong* seeds. Take thirty pills per dose.

Generally, the liver governs the eyes; the liver receives blood and thereby enables vision. If blood is weak, the liver’s *qi* lacks nourishment, and if the liver’s *qi* is not nourished, the gallbladder’s fluid cannot ascend. This leads to blurred vision in children, weak eyesight, and unclear perception of objects. This formula greatly nourishes liver blood, enriches gallbladder fluid, and dispels hidden obstructions in the eyes.

Take on an empty stomach with salted water to guide the formula downward. Take at midday with tea to clear the head and eyes. Take before bed with wine to nourish liver blood. For those who do not drink wine, take with a decoction of *renshen* (*Panax ginseng*) and *danggui* (*Angelica sinensis*). Prolonged use yields excellent results.

**For Various Red Eyes and Head-Wind with Red Swelling and Inability to Open the Eyes**
For pain from blows to the temples, this application is most effective.
- *Zhuya zaojiao* (*Gleditsia* thorns)
- *Huangbo* (*Phellodendron*)
- *Jianghuang* (*Turmeric*)
- *Nanxing* (*Arisaema*)
- *Caowu* (*Aconitum*)
- *Huanglian* (*Coptis*)

Grind into powder, mix with natural ginger juice, and apply to the temples. Pain ceases after one or two applications. Also suitable for red obstructions. For traumatic eye injuries with redness and swelling, add *furong* (*Hibiscus*) and *doufen* (*bean powder*), or apply mashed onion—both are effective.

**Wash for Various Eye Conditions**
- *Huanglian* (*Coptis*)
- *Danggui* (*Angelica sinensis*)
- *Chishaoyao* (*Paeonia lactiflora*)
- *Huashi* (*Talc*)

Grind into powder, steep in hot water, and let settle. Use the clear liquid to wash various types of corneal obstructions. Add *shigao* (*gypsum*), *ruxiang* (*frankincense*), and *qinpi* (*Fraxinus*) for festering wind. For *manxuan* wind, add *manjingzi* (*Vitex*) and *wubeizi* (*gallnut*), removing the core.

**Rehmannia Pill**
- *Juhua* (*Chrysanthemum*)
- *Muzei* (*Equisetum*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Cangzhu* (*Atractylodes*): 1 *liang*
- *Dihuang* (*Rehmannia*)
- *Gouqizi* (*Lycium* berries)
- *Jingjie* (*Schizonepeta*): 3 *qian*

Refine with honey into pills. Take twenty pills after meals with tea. Dispels wind and brightens vision; universally applicable for all conditions.

**Cuscuta Pill**
Calms the spirit, stabilizes the *po*, and brightens the eyes. Suitable for deficient eyes.
- *Shu qingpi* (*Citrus*, prepared): 1 *liang*
- *Cheqianzi* (*Plantago*): 1 *liang*
- *Baji* (*Morinda*, heart removed): 1 *liang*
- *Duzhong* (*Eucommia*, honey-fried until threads disappear): 1 *liang*
- *Weilingxian* (*Clematis*, wine-steeped): 1 *liang*
- *Yuan zhi* (*Polygala*, heart removed): 1 *liang*
- *Niuxi* (*Achyranthes*, wine-steeped): 1 *liang*
- *Congrong* (*Cistanche*, wine-steeped): 1 *liang*
- *Shu dihuang* (*Rehmannia*, prepared): 1 *liang*
- *Tusi* (*Cuscuta*): 2 *liang*

Steep the ingredients, then boil in wine and mix with flour paste to form pills. Take thirty pills on an empty stomach with salted wine.

**Three Yellows Decoction**
For sudden redness, swelling, and heat toxin.
- *Huanglian* (*Coptis*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Fuling* (*Poria*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Dahuang* (*Rheum*, roasted): 2 *liang*
- *Gancao* powder (*Glycyrrhiza*)
- *Poxiao* (*Mirabilite*)
- *Maimendong* (*Ophiopogon*)

Take after meals with hot water.

**Asarum Powder**
For trauma to the pupil with eye pain and bleeding.
- *Jingjiesui* (*Schizonepeta* spikes)
- *Cheqianzi* (*Plantago*)
- *Fuling* (*Poria*)
- *Xixin* (*Asarum*)
- *Digupi* (*Lycium* root bark): 3 *qian*
- A small amount of *moyao* (*myrrh*)

Take on an empty stomach with warm wine.

**Black Spirit Powder**
For women’s blood-wind festering eyes, postpartum menstrual irregularities with unbearable pain, or traumatic blood attacking the pupil. Disperses blood and dispels wind. **Do not take during pregnancy.**
- *Baimu* (*Paeonia lactiflora*, white)
- *Fuling* (*Poria*)
- *Gancao* (*Glycyrrhiza*)
- *Huixiang* (*Fennel*)
- *Rougui* (*Cinnamomum*)
- *Yuanhusuo* (*Corydalis*)
- *Sheng dihuang* (*Rehmannia*, raw)
- *Chuanxiong* (*Ligusticum*)
- *Shaoyao* (*Paeonia*)
- *Puhuang* (*Typha* pollen)
- *Muxiang* (*Aucklandia*)
- *Baizhi* (*Angelica dahurica*)
- *Danggui* (*Angelica sinensis*)

Grind into powder and take with wine.

**For Pterygium**
In the twelfth lunar month, use a male pig’s gallbladder, insert *mayaxiao* (*sodium sulfate*), and dry in the wind. Grind into powder, add *naozi* (*borneol*) and *shexiang* (*musk*), and apply.

**Processed Xuanning Powder**
Excellent for hot eyes and red eyes.
Take one yellow ox gallbladder, fill with 2 *qian* of pure *poxiao* (*Mirabilite*) and 1 *qian* of *huanglian* (*Coptis*), and hang in the wind. Daily, use a duck feather to brush off the crystallized *xia* from the outside of the gallbladder until exhausted. Collect in a ceramic jar and use as a standard eye drop.

**For Smallpox in Children**
Do not purge residual toxins. Only use *lü doupi* (*mung bean skin*) and *gujingcao* (*Eriocaulon*) in formulas. Avoid all other foods; regularly eating *luoshi* (*river snails*) is beneficial.

**For Smallpox Affecting the Eyes in Children**
Take *baishi* (*white persimmon*).

**For Measles Affecting the Eyes and Causing Corneal Opacities in Children**
- *Cao jueming* (*Cassia obtusifolia*)
- *Tianhuafen* (*Trichosanthes* root)
- *Gancao* (*Glycyrrhiza*)
- *Chishaoyao* (*Paeonia lactiflora*): each #4 *qian*

Grind into powder. Take 0.5 *qian* with boiled water.

**For Corneal Opacities**
- *Gualougen* (*Trichosanthes* root)
- *Gancao* (*Glycyrrhiza*)
- *Juemingcao* (*Cassia obtusifolia*)
- *Chishaoyao* (*Paeonia lactiflora*): each 0.5 *qian*

Mix with honey water and take.

**Cool Gan Pill**
For children’s *gan*-related red and festering eyes.
- *Kushen* (*Sophora*)
- *Fangfeng* (*Saposhnikovia*)
- *Manjingzi* (*Vitex*)
- *Longdancao* (*Gentiana*)
- *Xuanshen* (*Scrophularia*)

Grind into powder, form into pills the size of mung beans with pig’s bile paste, and take with tea.

**For Post-Measles Opacities on the Pupil**
- *Bai wuyi* (*Ulmus* fruit, peeled): 50 pieces
- *Ruireng* (*Prinsepia* kernels, peeled): 20 pieces
- *Lu hui* (*Aloe*): 3 *qian*
- *Xiongdan* (*bear’s gallbladder*): 3 *qian*

Grind the four ingredients finely, mix with 3 *liang* of raw sesame oil, and spread in a bowl. Apply as needed.

Next, take a piece of processed mugwort (*Artemisia argyi*) the size of a chicken egg, wrap it with one grain each of *dansha* (*cinnabar*), *ruxiang* (*frankincense*), and *pi* (*arsenic*), all finely ground and the size of soybeans. Place these inside the mugwort, then burn it to fumigate the medicine in the bowl until the mugwort is fully consumed. Remove and grind finely, then apply a dose the size of a millet grain to the eye.

**Frequent-Wash Formula**
For all types of wind-heat, heart-heat, wind-toxin festering canthi, redness, roughness, itching, pain, obstructions, nebulae, and blood-wind conditions in women.
- *Wubeizi* (*Galla Chinensis*), sifted of dust
- *Manjingzi* (*Vitex*), white skin removed, washed in hot water

Grind into powder. For each dose, take 2 *qian*, place in a sand pot with half a cup of water and thirty to fifty copper coins. Seal the mouth with paper, heat over fire for a long time, then pierce a small hole in the paper to let the steam fumigate the eyes. When the temperature is tolerable, pour out the clear liquid and wash the eyes while warm. Stop when cool, then reheat and wash again.

**Another Wash Formula**
- *Tongqing* (*verdigris*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Baiqiantu* (*kaolin*): 1 *liang*
- *Wubeizi* (*Galla Chinensis*): 1.5 *qian*

Grind together into powder, steep in hot water, and wash the eyes while hot with eyes closed. Do not let the medicine enter the eyes. Stop when cool, then reheat and wash again. Suitable for all festering canthi.

**Tea-Blended Powder**
For men and women with all types of wind-swelling, itching, pain, nebulae, festering canthi, *qi*-induced tearing, and blurred vision.
- *Chuanxiong* (*Ligusticum*)
- *Fangfeng* (*Saposhnikovia*)
- *Qianghuo* (*Notopterygium*): each 1 *liang*
- *Gancao* (*Glycyrrhiza*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Muzei* (*Equisetum*)
- *Shigao* (*gypsum*), stir-fried
- *Shijueming* (*abalone shell*), calcined
- *Jingjie* (*Schizonepeta*)
- *Boheye* (*Mentha*)
- *Ganjuhua* (*Chrysanthemum*): each 1 *liang*

Grind into powder. Take 2 *qian* per dose, mixed with tea.

**For All Heat-Induced Eye Conditions**
First, take 4 *liang* of *Huanglian* (*Coptis*), slice, and decoct into a thick paste. Then, take one large sweet melon, cut open the top, scrape out the seeds, and layer with fresh *Bohe* (*Mentha*) and *Mayaxiao* (*sodium sulfate*), filling the melon completely. Replace the top and hang in a windy place for three to four days. The *xiaoshao* will crystallize on the melon’s skin; brush it off daily with a goose feather and mix evenly with the *Huanglian* paste. Store in a white vessel and apply to hot eyes.

**Plaster for Red and Hot Eyes**
- *Sangye* (*Morus leaf*): 2 *liang*
- *Jingjie* (*Schizonepeta*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Poxiao* (*sodium sulfate*): 2 *liang*
- *Dahuang* (*Rheum*): 0.5 *liang*

Grind into powder, mix with honey water, and apply to the *taiyang* acupoints to reduce heat and blood.

**Purple Gold Pill**
A secret formula for eye conditions.
- *Chuanxiong* (*Ligusticum*): 1.5 *liang*
- *Danggui* (*Angelica sinensis*): 1.5 *liang*
- *Chushi* (*Broussonetia fruit*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Bohe* (*Mentha*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Gualougen* (*Trichosanthes root*): 6 *qian*
- *Manjingzi* (*Vitex*), stir-fried: 2 *liang*
- *Chuanjiao* (*Zanthoxylum*), seeds removed and baked: 1.5 *liang*
- *Ganjuhua* (*Chrysanthemum*): 3 *qian*
- *Mimenghua* (*Buddleja*): 3 *qian*
- *Shepi* (*snake slough*), soaked: 3 *qian*
- *Jingjiesui* (*Schizonepeta spike*), soaked: 3 *qian*
- *Digupi* (*Lycium bark*): 1 *liang*

The above four ingredients should be soaked in *Gancao* (*Glycyrrhiza*) juice, then baked dry.
- *Baijili* (*Tribulus*), spines removed and soaked: 1.5 *liang*

Grind the thirteen ingredients into fine powder, mix with refined honey, and form into pills weighing 1 *qian* each. Take with the appropriate adjuvant:
- For dim, bluish nebulae: with *Danggui* wine
- For *qi*-induced obstructions: with *Muxiang* (*Aucklandia*) decoction
- For women’s blood dizziness: with *Danggui* and *Bohe* decoction

There was a man whose eyes were affected by heat from drinking alcohol, leaving him unable to distinguish paths for three years. After taking this medicine for twenty-five days, he saw improvement. Another, whose eyes were harmed by *qi* and had been dim for eight years without light, took this medicine for forty days and saw improvement, regaining clarity after sixty days. Yet another, who had lost sight for four years after the death of his mother, took this medicine for fifty days and recovered his former clarity.

**Another Formula**
For all types of eye conditions with nebulae, obstructions, and dimness, highly effective.
- *Chuanxiong* (*Ligusticum*): 1.5 *liang*
- *Danggui* (*Angelica sinensis*): 1.5 *liang*
- *Gualougen* (*Trichosanthes root*), raw: 6 *qian*
- *Chuanjiao* (*Zanthoxylum*), seeds removed: 7 *qian*
- *Chushi* (*Broussonetia fruit*), seeds removed and lightly stir-fried: 0.5 *liang*
- *Gancao* (*Glycyrrhiza*): 3 *qian*
- *Ganjuhua* (*Chrysanthemum*): 1 *liang*
- *Shetui* (*snake slough*): 3 *qian*
- *Huanglian* (*Coptis*): 3 *qian*
- *Manjingzi* (*Vitex*): 1 *liang*
- *Muzei* (*Equisetum*), soaked in boys’ urine overnight and baked dry: 1 *liang*
- *Bohe* (*Mentha*): 0.5 *liang*
- *Mimenghua* (*Buddleja*): 1 *liang*
- *Digupi* (*Lycium bark*): 1 *liang*
- *Qianghuo* (*Notopterygium*): 1 *liang*
- *Baixianhua* (*Dictamnus*): 1 *liang*
- *Banxingjie* (*Schizonepeta*): 1 *liang*

Grind the sixteen ingredients into powder, mix with refined honey, and form into pills. Take one *liang* divided into ten pills, twice daily after meals. Adjuvants:
- For those with *#5*: with rice-washed water
- For dim eyes: with *Danggui* decoction
- For *qi*-induced obstructions: with *Muxiang* (*Aucklandia*) decoction
- For women’s blood dizziness: with *Bohe* and *Danggui* decoction

Avoid raw, fishy, alcoholic, and damp foods. This medicine has proven repeatedly effective.

**For Heat-Wind Eyes**
Take an unspecified quantity of *Dongqingzi* (*Ilex fruit*), crush to extract juice, and simmer into a paste. Strain thoroughly, store in a porcelain jar, and bury underground for seven days to remove fire-toxin. Use to apply to hot eyes.

**Another Formula**
Take 4 *liang* each of *Huanglian* (*Coptis*) and *Poxiao* (*sodium sulfate*), decoct in plain water into a paste, and apply to hot eyes.

**Another Formula**
Take carp gallbladder juice warm and apply.

**For Severely Festering Canthi**
First wash with *Wubeizi* (*Galla Chinensis*) and *Manjingzi* (*Vitex*). Then take 2 *liang* of *Luganshi* (*smithsonite*), calcine in fire, and quench seven or eight times with *Huanglian* (*Coptis*) juice and boys’ urine. Grind finely, then add 5 *qian* of *Tongqing* (*verdigris*), 1 *qian* of *Pengsha* (*borax*), a small amount of *Shexiang* (*musk*), and 0.5 *qian* of *Yaxiao* (*sodium sulfate*). Grind into fine powder and apply to the canthi.

**For Infants Under One Year Old with Red Eyes**
Grind *Huanglian* (*Coptis*) into powder, mix with tea, and apply to the palms and soles. This will cure the condition. If swelling and pain make it difficult to open the eyes, add *Jianghuang* (*turmeric*), *Zaojiao* (*Gleditsia*), and *Poxiao* (*sodium sulfate*), grind into powder, and apply to the *taiyang* acupoints and palms and soles. Adding scallions and applying as a poultice is even more effective.

*End of Scroll Eleven of the Immortal’s Transmitted External Medicine Secret Formulas*

The character "久" in the manuscript copy appears as "还."
The character "各" here likely has missing text following it.
The character "医" is suspected to be a scribal error for "翳."
